Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the patient who dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse in the way we have said through the divisions of cures, and it does not benefit, then three manners of cauterization are added that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Here is the translation:
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After I insert the two inflamed nerves so that the key is perceived from the other side, and then drive forth the cautery, and thus there will be four; if you see, then cauterize the entire cautery to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when he has taken pollution for long time, and this is true of the other cures before mentioned.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery does not benefit an humpbacked person, except in the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the manners we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations around the mouth, one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the womb, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in front of the breast; and let the cauterizations be well close to the place where the key.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the cautery open to generate purpuration for a long time, and do not neglect the cure of the patient after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the bone that we showed before; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is placed here.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical, and are full of yellowish dew, it is necessary that you cauterize above the heel of the foot between the wristbone and the anklebone; and lift your hand with the cautery so as to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into the fontanelle, thus the yellowish dew might be stirred up, and the cautery should be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After make two cauters on each leg, one at the tip of the cuticular and the other below the knee in front and behind, inside the leg; and let the cauters stay open for a long time without healing, until the yellowish moisture comes out; after the cure of the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by manner of cures; and you see the patient well suffering and having strong virtue, then make one great cautery on the stomach according to what was said before about the stomach's cautery, at the circulatory cautery; and three cauters around the belly subtle as each individual bone is subtle, and two cauters on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the knuckle, and one cautery on each elbow, and two small cauters on the stomach below the great one, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, one or more, and are old and consist of large, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, if you make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that one which is entirely below almecdate peccant little by little in triangulating, and one cautery under the jawbone two digits; and if you think that his stomach is refrigerated, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swelling, then one makes a great cautery on the stomach, as was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen for all the cauterization nail-like; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After care, let the limb remain until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the fleshiness called "thelul", if you scrape off the cauterized part that looks like a rasp, and then put all ablaze on the cauterized part of the fleshiness cut; and leave it so long as the cauteries come to the opening of the vein, so that the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much fleshiness, then cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of ointments, profiting until they are healed; and if you cauterize a great fire on the flesh, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an untimely wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes such a disease that it cannot be healed except by fire cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes forth, and is swollen and discharges pus and corrupt moisture, then you must prove the depth of the entire tent, and make sure that you know how deep it is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After sharpen the cautery which seems like a scraper, and plug it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and continue the cautery until those corrupt and putrid parts are burned away, once or twice or three times, depending on the amount needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes into the body of the bladder and intestine, then beware of those places, and do not make fires except in a charred area, and think that it is not a peril; after care, let the limb remain until it is healed, and if the places are softened, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the place is entirely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is troubled, and the bone is corrupted in its depth; and thus as one of those things we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys and great windiness, and does not take on a womanly appearance, then it is necessary that you make a fire cauterization on the kidneys from one side and the other at the nails of fire cauterization as we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a fire cauterization on the outside of the part where the hair begins to grow on the pubic area, and one on each side, and each be as long as the nail of a thumb; and make one cauterization on the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizations be nails according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the membranes
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the membranes are cold and moist, and do not allow conception to occur, and the flowers are corrupted and their term is delayed; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that you make three cauterizations around the mouth, as we have said for the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and let the cauterizations be nails, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the hip of the thigh, and because of this it moves out of its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and there is found the wound of the departure, so it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip of the thigh with a cauterization resembling a circle, and sign before the wound around the hip as it turns, so that the hip be inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those which have been cauterized in the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, make three great fire cauterizations on the olive-shaped part, and let the cauterizations be as deep as all the keys; and cure him so that he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip of the thigh, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient has been cured with what we have said in the division, but the cure does not hold, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick humors with foul pills or other good-looking pills similar to them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is thus according to two manners: that is to know together burning medicines and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is thus according to many manners, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the back of the haunch three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good profundity and great, and have between each cautery the width of a thumb, and be the cauteries oval-shaped; sometimes done in the middle above the head of the haunch, wherefore there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the fire of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in this manner so that the circles contain all the hip, and all the keys of the cure be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain stays in the haunch and does not reach as far as the hip or as far as the knee.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the hip and the knee, make two cauteries on either side where the patient says the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle four thumb-widths away to the left; and let the cauteries be knife-like, and let the thickness of the keratin be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as the two feet or almost up to it, make three or four cauteries where they feel the pain, which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more of them; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make a cauterization at the knife-like or circular cauterization, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had a fire cauterization on the ankle of the foot, and they were left so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the belly which led to his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, do a cauterization on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sages say in the cauterization of the groin, this is how it is done, make such an iron and be as big at the top as a walnut of dactyl, or one pomegranate less, and be three quarters of an inch between them and be just enough to fit the quantity of a new pea; and the spaces should be about two parts, and they should also be like beans, and there should be enough iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its regard, and if we see little who uses it; and yet all the same it is one of the good cauteries which can be suffered, and where it applies itself.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine burning are such that you make an instrument between two things in which the edges of the door descend, and it is made of earth or iron to a length of one pace long, and on top it has three knobs, and each knob has the quantity of the size of a dove; and they are open at the front and back, and come together as one according to this form.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After put the bunch of hay under the patient lying on their side, and then put your hand on top of the bunch of hay; afterwards pour hot water between the two circles that has been heated in a pot at one point, and let it be for an hour or time, and allow the patient to feel the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds a mordication as if from fire; and when the mordications are gone, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hot poultice away, and let it be in this way for three days, and put on butter until what is blackened by the scabbing is removed; and after three days when corruption ceases to progress; and that would be the final aid after the treatment of ointments as long as they are healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the hip or leg, make the instrument that holds it in place according to what you have done in a similar way; and this is the method of the hot water, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot water, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new vessel.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	or there is a small hole at the bottom so that the point of a razor can fit into it; and put this pot on top of another well-balanced pot, and place hot water, sweet water above, until you have two layers of powder on top as you will then hold it in your hand; and leave it like that until the water has dripped down to the bottom pot, then take all the water and pour it onto the hot water and alkali just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	Et lors si sera much anguish and administered in the movements of medicine and fires; for it works like fire, and also on other medicines that are well cauterized, such as henna, tissoe, and myrrh with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us about a treatment whose man was cured of the pain in his groin and sciatic vein, and he greatly praised it, saying that no other treatment was done, and he became whole again at just one time when this treatment was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same way that you take fresh and dry verdigris, and grind it much with a small amount of grease, and put it on the groin, thigh, and leg where the pain holds, and bind it; and leave it there for three hours so that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath until his body is somewhat warmed, and make him enter into bed, and the pain will depart entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cautery of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's gall, it helps a lot; and the cauteries should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the other one called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take goat's gall in its dry form, and put it on the fire until it is charcoal, and place it on the linen, and let it be there until it cools down; and do it again like this, and do not stop doing it like this as long as you think by sense that he will come to the hainche, and that the pain will cease; and this manner of cauterization is called "cautere de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain from the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or from excessive blood evacuation, or from similar signs of cold matter expanded, none of these similarities is worth cauterizing, unless it comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be freed from fetid pills or other similar things, and that one is applied to their back, where the pain persists, three lines marked with a lead, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauterization be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see fit, make .iij. cauteries or .iiij. at the middle nail-shaped cautery in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight and narrow back when they wake up, and fear; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and in the appearance which appears above other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you can cure it, then cauterize at the point called "celcle" according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cauterizes each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that it is being cauterized around the spine by the fire for 2 or 3 lines, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply fire cauterization to a hollow or bony part which may be near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain from joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain from joints is due to moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which doctors properly call "podagre", and when it is caused by cold and medicines do not cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the jointure of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the surface of the foot, then let the fire cauterize all over the area where we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knee and other joints, and this happens many times, then let the fire cauterize on each knee three or four cauterizations per part, all over the olive-shaped area; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand there longer than until the flesh of the wound is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the groin and back, administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make punctures around the wrist II lines; and if there remains no pain at all to the shoulders, make punctures above each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just to the armpits or just to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good governance to the patient and provide medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed with the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the pitch
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the running comes in sores, and the boils descend to the groin and it is newly, then it is necessary that when you see it curing, it does not waste the day; and that he uses things which loosen the belly, so that the wind descends from his belly; after this make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the boil is repaired, and then lead him back to your side, and mark with a lead under the running sore on the bone of the elbow, and at all one sign which is similar to half a circle above the body; then apply the cautery in this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he is pale and produces stools.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reposition the bowels to their place; and the attendants hold his hand above so that they do not return backward; and work well on the patient's hips, and put a cushion and a servant under him, and another one on the chest holding his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of all your fingers, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you don't reach it the first time, do it again another time until you reach the bone; and beware subtly so that the bowel does not burst when you do the cautery; nor burn him; and lest by this the patient die or suffer other evils.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach just to the bone at the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their measure, and those of great people also great according to their measure; after three days, cure with butter at the site of the cautery until the scabbing is removed; after curing other ointments until they are healed, and have the patient lie down on his back for 40 days so that the wound may be well closed; and it is necessary that their bandages be worn long enough, so that the boil does not burst when he will want to go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, let a well-made bandage be applied to him, and wear it for another 40 days; and have good rest, that he trouble himself little and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and loud shouting; and when he has followed this instruction, then he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say next about the cutting treatment in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the running of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come to other bodies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make the fire cautery of the same kind according to its quantity, and let the third part of the flesh be burned; after the cure as we have said; and none of the ancients have said one should cauterize at the cautery into three angles in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the joint and make a line above the ulcer for its width, and another below, and then with your hand fill in all the cauterizing.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are more gentle and moist.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, either from falling or hitting, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine is of no use, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauterization be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and virtue, and its location regarding torsions and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cauterization, it's well; if not, start another cauterization on that one, because such custom is that it should be changed to the member that is closest, so you must do the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	A surgery.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The swelling is aided sometimes by cauterization with great help, and likewise the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you not see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not relapse or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread to the whole patient, then make V cauterizations on the head: one in the middle of the head up to nine, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the hatterel; and leave your hand so that the cauterization reaches just to the bone, and until the rinds come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the surgery is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize those cauterizations on the head that we have said, and one cauterization in the navel, and two cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and six cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one large one on the groin and another below, and two on each shoulder; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take care of the nerves that are on the back surface, so you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cauterization on the bone of the arm, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I do of cauterizing, the more it helps and brings benefit; and know that patients do not feel pain from cauterizing as much as healthy people do, because the body is already quite corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that cauterizations be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, wash the wound with flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, ointments, and poultices, but it is not healed, then make cauterizations on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little bit deep into the flesh of the wound; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes one makes a cautery to the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is removed the swelling; but however no one intervenes unless they are familiar with the members and the issues of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine is of no use, then cauterize it with one cautery slightly deep, according to the quantity of the flesh of the limb, until the pus is removed, and its color changes; then cure with flour mixed with honey and lentils, and oil of roses and leaves of plantain, and blood of hen and blood of almond, each in a part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancres by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning and you see it arrested, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen some time ago; and it is more right that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati" and it tars to die or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the old age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood or because of the weather; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it with many small cauteries in piercing; afterwards let it be thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the cauterization, then heat the cauterization until it takes on its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the core, and be such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in this manner as the course of the purging is eased.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterward, care for it until he is healed perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a devouring of member, for it devours the members just as fire consumes dry reeds.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can bear fire cautery together, then prepare the cauterizers both large and small, according to what is needed at the place where the disease is; afterwards, cauterize all around until you remove all corruption, and nothing remains, so that everything that is corrupted may be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized areas a poultice with oil as long as the scorching of fire is removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment by unguents produces flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not arise, it is good; and if not, then re-cauterize on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy has sometimes been cured by medication in place of fire cauterization; but nonetheless fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medication in its division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of boils that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Much of a time it happens that on feet by default there is born a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a great swelling needed which hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is so according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery iron to the point where it can burn all around, and has fine edges; afterwards, you place it all over the clot, and turn your hand completely around the clot until it comes to the bottom of the clot; and then leave it thus for three days until it begins to suppurate; then apply a poultice made from wild malve roots mixed with oil, and let the poultice stay on all night, and the clot will fall off and be removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with oil, anointing it until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if it is converted by external ulcers on the body, and often occurs in hands and feet, then you should bring hot water cautery to it; and do this: take a cane of clay or iron, or a feather from a vulture, and place it on the ulcer and the surrounding area, that is to say, pores or small holes; and place the cane so that it surrounds everything, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand by turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the ulcer, and then the hot water will find its way down to the root; and allow the patient a little time for the hot water's cauterization to last about an hour; then leave it like this, and it will fall off all at once with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Sores are dealt with similarly, as long as you gather up all those that are on the body, then cure the swellings that cause flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for shakiness
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people shake from chilliness or fever quartan or another, it is necessary that you make four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the weight, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if the shaking will cease, and the health of the cold illness will hasten.
des pustules puans	of stinking pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No matter what appears on the surface of the washed body or pustules that stink, which come from great corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	Then it is necessary to do a first treatment when they appear, making a fire cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization of myrtle wood, by which the point should be seized by fire, or a long aristolochia root, or a lenticular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And no matter what, when you cauterize them at the beginning, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further forward, but are broken down the superfluities from which they come, and are cleansed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great hemorrhaging of blood comes from the artery that is cut off at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a member, and similar things; and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And although this happens to someone, if you hurry and put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tightly until the blood is stilled beneath your fingers, and no more drips out; then take up the olive cauteries, many small and great ones, until they are all red; then grasp one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery runs, and put it on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cauterize so that the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts forth when you lift your fingers off the vein, and the cauterize is extinguished, then take up quickly another of the cauterizes that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing these one after another until the blood is staunched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, one cannot well staunch it, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of the three ways we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong binding with thread, or by medicines put on which have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and held in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will instruct the patient to staunch with a tight binding of cloths or by placing burning things on it, or other similar things, unless they are not beneficial.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he does not have a mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it tightly until it is staunched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often when it is very cold, so that the blood may congeal and swell and be staunched; and make preparations for what he needs of cauterizers and medicines ahead.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all illnesses where it is necessary to cauterize with fire or burning medicine, and the questions and causes and preparations and forms of cauterizations; and I have placed that chapter from top to bottom, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way so that what one wants to find may be found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and therefore it is necessary to take greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come to treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who have so harmed themselves with their illness that they will die quickly due to the severity of their disease and the greatness of their wickedness; and one should fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who will give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting for you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not foolishly act on mere guesses, but wisely about what you are certain of and can grasp; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your patients, so that salvation may be converted; and this will help you to achieve good renown, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, May Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter in sections, as is before the section of cauterizers, that I have arranged from top to bottom, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often befalls children during childbirth, and when the woman holds the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and all those that I have seen hastened death; and therefore it seems to me that it would be pointless to continue the work on such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head was swelling each day until it could no longer be supported; and so much moisture accumulated that it seemed to be dead, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone above the sphenoid, between the skull and the bone; and the work is such that when the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you make a cut in the head, making a wide incision; and it should be as long as two noses, as long as the moisture flows.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and you see signs that the commissures of the head are open on each part, and the liquid jumps forth when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not respond to you: so it is necessary to make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after incising, extract all moisture forth.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After binding the wounds with cloths and powders, and putting wine and oil, and leaving it thus until the fifth day; then unbind, and treat the wound by tents and anointings, and let the head be drained evenly, and thereafter feed the patient dry food without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where the opening of the abscess is, and the gathering of the liquid; for sometimes it is before; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the place where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the liquid, and the flesh as far as you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and if there is bleeding of blood, so that the patient may die from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of pus
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarre" in the eye or at the liver, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last remedy is the fire cauterization with those that will cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you wish to clean the head, it is necessary for the patient to lower their head; after which, scrape the area with a rough cloth so that the arteries appear, then have the patient pull back their neck to the whole cloth; then look if the vein bleeds, and the veins of one and the other are afterwards behind the ears, and they are repointed; then mark the veins with ink, then cut one and the other with an acicular spatula of two parts, so that the cut comes just to the bone, and this should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting as two should be across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood springs out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Et if the artery does not open to feeling, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space between three bones; then sign and fill up just to the bone; and as for what it is necessary to do with blood, it is six c/, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone, point out where the syphac lies; then cut off that apostema lest it not be, then strain the wound and bind, and the ointment cure until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraines come and sharp catarrhs, due to moistures of tears and heats in temples and soothed ancient forgetfulness and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medical cures and yet all this does not help, then we cut off the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have counted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient turns back the hairs of his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is hardly responsive except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responsive, then pull out the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and raise the liquid of hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the skin slightly until you come to the artery, then take it up to the pincers, and depart well from the threads that are below each part; and if the artery is thin, then turn it to the point of the awl, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Since she isn't cut open, the blood does not flow at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take out the blood of .vi. c/, up to .iii.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double strong silk thread, so that no bleeding will occur before the wound is healed, and blood will flow decoratively; then cut off the excess that is between the two ligatures at that same hour, and then, if you see, cauterize the area with the cutlery cauterizer up to the bone until the veins are cut; and this is the true work, if the patient has no fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cauterization is aid to finish off moistures: for this reason it is more helpful against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that you fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made tents; and when you remove them, be careful with dry medicines that produce flesh, and with tents, until he is healed; and if the artery bleeds so much as you work on it, hasten to cauterize by fire, or apply the place with vitriol and strain it with your hand until the bleeding subsides; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on the place until the bleeding ceases, and raise the place with cold water until the bleeding stops, and be strained as necessary; and what is true and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this fire cauterizer cutting to two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to withstand more heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the cuttings are too close together, they retain their heat less well.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have one large space between the two cutters, and then when you have marked from end to end the two places, take the burning iron and apply it so that it reaches up to the bone, and cut off the vein in two places; and be separated between the two veins because they are not sewn together by this cauterization entirely; and this is the form of the cauterizer:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead of the head below, and medical treatment does not help, and you see the patient's face growing red, and feel a burning sensation on the forehead as if it were trembling; and the oils are hot and moist so that the hairs of the papers have fallen out, and the papers are scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to use this cure.
