Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the old "contused cure", and this is what you do for the patient with this disease: make three cuts on the forehead, even and equal in length according to the length of the forehead; and one of the cuts should be like two fingers deep within the forehead, going down towards the nose, and the other two should be two finger-widths above the eyebrows, and take care not to cut into the arteries that are above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and each wound should be three finger-widths across when traversing the joints; and prepare a piece of sponge and many cloths so that the blood can flow, then pour in the absorbent liquid, carefully making sure it's the right shape.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is above the temple up to the second incision; and scrape out all the membrane that is between the two cuts as far as the surface of the bone, then make another part from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	so put the instrument called "culterelle" into the first incision; and it is very well cutting on one side, and not cutting on the other side, and that's its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the edge of the blade cutting towards the seared flesh at the heart, and the edge soft towards the bone, and blunt it until it comes to the main cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to what appears at the heart, and then make another part in the main cut up to the other side; and then extract blood evenly, and express the place where the blood has been taken; then put a linen cloth in each cut, and cover with moistened cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar, and guard against abscesses coming there; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer great quantities of lukewarm water, then apply basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with a burning in the eyes as usual, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and weakening the sight, and the papers burnt; and the hair falling out, and the head deep in pain, and the patient is exhausted; then you know by these accidents that those matters and that burning do not come from one voice alone, but from many voices, and the true cure that is there, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to return his forehead, then make a great cut in the forehead, and another of moderate size.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision all the way to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples' veins that move at mealtime; and when the bone is exposed, let all the blood flow into a sponge, then dry it between the two lips of the cut and put old cotton and linen there; then place damp cloths soaked in wine and oil above, and take care not to form a warm abscess; when it's removed, you should rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with caustic things that make flesh become inflamed.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flower and three parts of aloes, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds in order to inflame flesh everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of three things: either grains, or beasts, or pieces of rock or similar things like iron; or seeds, such as millet, beans, peas; or flowing things, such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it happens in the ear or some other way that does not belong to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a little bit of violet oil or sesame oil, and then apply extraction; and when the purging comes forth, plug the nose with condiment, and stop up the nostrils when the purging arrives, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes forth by this treatment; and if it does not come forth, apply extraction with fine tweezers, of which there is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the tweezers, that's good; if not, then administer an extraction with a fine thread of small double wire; and if it doesn't jump out in this way, then make a chain of iron and put the head of the chain or the ear canal strongly, and stop what is around the chain with beeswax so that the blood cannot enter with the chain; then treat it forcefully, for many times it works as we have said; and if it doesn't work in this way, then take glue from which birds are taken, and put in some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and wrap a little cotton around; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is, and treat it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't jump out from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear in such a way that an abscess forms and swells; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient well with cephalic ointment, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or bone depends; and let the incision be like a moon, as long as you can reach the stone, then cut it out according to your ability, and suck it hastened to your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grain that is in there and it swells, then administer an extraction; and if it can't come out, then administer one subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and apply an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tweezers and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction be light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water then that falls in the ear it is necessary for the patient to use purging with condiment first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be held on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps forth because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of the stick you should hold tight and light, and heat them with fire; and put the patient's ear into one or two perforations in his ear, and step back from the other side, and pierce another stone on top of the ear-stone; and do not cease doing this stone by stone until all the water comes out, and thus she will jump out completely; and if you see, take a tendril, and put one head into the ear, and the other head takes fire as long as the most tender tendril is burned; then redo with another set of tendril-some things as many times as the water comes out, just as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	En the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, such as a mouse and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel it, then use forceps extraction; and this is the thing easier to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of lice from the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then it is necessary to look at the ear to the sun: if any lice appear, then treat them with fine forceps; and if they do not appear, take a thread whose form this is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And bind the most subtle thread in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed strongly at all the cord; do this often until all the threads come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then stop around the cord with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, then administer distillations which the ancients have proved in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or treat the distillations; and then distill your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, for which there is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or tin, narrow below to one small hole, and wide above for distilling; and for pressing within the distillation with one instrument of well-made tin, and if you see, take a rasp and wrap it around the point pleasantly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice into the canal, and that which you see of your medicines in the thread, and the thread should be in the ear; then push down into the rasp all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or flows from the ear; and if the patient feels it inside, and it is a small pot heated over the fire so that one can distill in the ear; and take care not to let it be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by stopping of wound, or new growth within the ear, and these stoppings sometimes occur very deep in the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes there is a small pot that fills up the hole, and it can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes very deep, if one cannot see it, is of grievous inflammation in many dispositions, and that which can be seen requires that you put the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see apparent thickening, then work with all this spatula whose form this is.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and cutting in front and back all plain, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the thickening is of new flesh or cartilage of the ear, then hold it with fine forceps, and cut lightly, until that cartilage is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the pustules are open very far in the ear, then take a subtle, light rasp and heat it slightly on the fire, then put it in the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense the impaction that the patient feels grief at hearing, pierce lightly, and beware that you do not harm the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten it with Egyptian oil.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder on vitriol broom; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and put another moist tent made of roset oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if hemorrhage comes from the wound, then plunge an absorbent and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the hemorrhage which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This all that comes out of paper from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to stretch with tenaille and forceps, and cut off at a spatula of its roots; then put on the place vitriol broom.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they flake off without a core, then cauterize with the lenticular cautery, and after the incision it moves; and many times repair, but no part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the Grisle (a type of wax)
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to the eyes in papers things that seem like hail in their form and hardness, and therefore this disease is called "grandine", and it is an accumulation of moisture thick on the paper above and below; the procedures are such: beware if the grandine moves from one part to another, and it's a light thing to know; then make the donation of the width, then peel each part lightly, then take out with tweezers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you can't cut it without piercing the paper slightly, then don't harm anything to the patient; and if the wound is large, assemble a stitch and cure until it is healed; and if it's small, don't do anything forcefully, for the ointments will restore it quickly and smooth out the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending from the inner ear to the upper part, then turn the paper over, and extract the grandine with fine forceps, and cut and press on both sides; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it will not harm anything; and when the grandine is cut, pour salted water into the ear, and cure the place where flesh grows forth until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is smeared on pieces of paper above, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and greatly distresses them; and they come with catharrhe in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie down on their faces again, and sleep on top, and their papers are moist beneath their eyelids, covered by the swelling and appearance that has hidden the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your elbow to your breast and feel the exinach between.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts their head in your hand; and then take one linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach from each part, then put it on them; and press with your fingers on both sides, so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle; then make a cut in the middle of the moisture with a spatula, cutting a slit of the width, but not more than the wound one makes to heal a vine; and make the skin very thin until you come to the exinach; and in several dispositions comes the exinach from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white grease.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Here is the translation:
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the hernia does not open at the beginning of the tear, so slightly widen the tear until it appears; then pull it as we have said, then moisten cloths in warm water and cold water, and place them on the area, and hold steady with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who burn themselves and put it on top in order to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it until it is cleansed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess comes to a boil, then the cure with soothing poultices continues until it is cleansed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of paper grow, other than those that are natural, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes and cause ways of illnesses such as tears, softening of the paper, and whitening, until it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes; and there is care according to four manners: or by fire cautery together, or by medicinal water as described in the chapter on cautery, and this is done either by incision and sewing or by cauterization, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your shoulder; then turn the paper of oil towards your left hand; if it has converted, it is good; if not, put an awl into each thread above; and let this be at the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow among these hairs, and lead one thread above to all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs that are adjacent, all the spatula copulating from the great tear to the small; then draw out one thread, and place beneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth; then sign on the paper a figure of anointing, like the leaf of myrtle, and yet it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevating the paper which is divided in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et si aueil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantite de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des loü grant larmier jusque petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles du keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille à tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai àerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz à tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusque III jours ou IV; puis cure la plaie sans costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sans paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi comme li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, à III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what goes above the small threads equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and things are not equal, take a needle where there is thread, and put it in the figure; and put the other thread near the great incision, and the second thread near the small one, and join the two threads equally between your hands; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above what you have marked, as we have counted, then join the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with ointment and similar soothing unguents; and sometimes it happens that the hairs on the paper are converted: so it is necessary to use what we have said about incising; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of cauterization is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole in it according to what I have said, and then make two cauterizations by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut off the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what goes above the paper of oil, and strain the two cauterizations from the two parties together; and let it be like this for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and decay and fall off, until it falls away by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time, if the pus has formed some strength, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper is lifted, and they can no longer be pinched by the hairs; and this is the shape of the two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine awl, and put one thread of silk into it and make it soft and subtle; then assemble the ends and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be as long as a palm; then arrange another fine thread of silk briefly, and tie the head of the thread; then place the patient's head on your shoulder; and be below the sun so that the work is declared, for this is a subtle and gentle work; then put the awl into all the chase in the root of the adjacent hair, and make it pierce the paper quickly until you reach the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the chase, and put that hair into the chase if there is one, two, three, or more; then pull your hand away until the hairs come forth to all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull out the chase from below to all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes forth from the pores above and you see it by the sight of the eye; then pull out the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh rises; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural horse's mane, and be elevated with that which you leave, as long as it is elongated and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's purging
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" comes to the eye, so there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden wound, or cutting, or burning, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to work on it is that you cut open this wound, and separate its lips, and put inside linen cloths, and tie it until it heals; and it's not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry out and tighten.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, then the illness will return worse than the first; but using soft things, such as fenugreek; and marshmallow or hawthorn fruit cooked, and oil of lilyflower melted in some oil, and wrap it with a cloth, and cure it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care to ensure it does not heal unequally according to its former form; and these works that we have said are not other than remedies for this disease, so that it may return according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is below which is truly called "axacrati" and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental comes from wound and cutting and cautery and similar things; and the way of working is that you take a needle with double thread, and thrust it into the flesh, and make it pierce from left to right until it comes out on the other side, so that the threads come together in two holes of the flesh; then leave the flesh above all the needle, and cut at the spatula, being wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper comes back as it should, that's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or innermost within the paper; and be the holes of the two cuts at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape will be like the shape of a letter which has no name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges is grown under, from what follows the paper; then join the two parted parts with a linen thread; then apply the cure of what we have said of softening medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from gash or seam or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the treatment according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an instrument for every possible way that it may return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden removal of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture has been done in the same way as the paper above is sewn with white of egg, and it cannot move nor perform its natural actions, then it is necessary that you put the point of a rasp underneath the paper and lift it up; and let it be so pinched, until you cut what is at the subtle spatula, which is not too worn away nor too torn, so that the patient cannot endure having the spatula too worn away or blinding the eye; and your incision, from which you remove this assembled part, should be slightly done, so that the paper may return to its natural form; and let all this assembled part heal, and sometimes do something in the water, and raise it with sweet water, and vinegar; then put between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye a moist linen cloth, and after three days use the colic remedy and similar things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the eyelash is in two manners: it is nervy and resembles a hard scaly skin, and another which is not nervy, but resembles white congealed moisture, which when one touches it with iron and cools it with pincers, cannot be handled; and both appearances begin at the great temple and grow slowly by degrees until it covers all the sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then opens their eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then cools the eyelash with pincers of small double-edged scissors, and lifts it up; then take an awl, and put one hair from a horse, or ox, or buffalo, and a strong thread; and double the point of the awl a little and insert it into the eyelash, and pierce all the way to the entire awl, and tie the eyelash with a thread and lift it up, and scrape away everything that is on the side of the eyelash from the prune and the silk to the hair tip; then cut off what remains in the root of the temple at the subtle spatula and small forces, and leave the natural skin or the eyelid, so that through the incision the body's tears do not come forth as usual; and sometimes the eyelashes are only set on the needle and thread, as we have said; then scrape everything off the entire soft spatula from which is the form.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the prune is not pierced; and after the incision, pour a little bit of boiled silk into the eye, and make a colic remedy with litargyrum, and leave it until the next day; then apply the cure for what needs to be done until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the eyelash is not nervy and you cannot insert the awl, and the needle cannot enter, then this appearance of eyelash is cured with medicines; and it grows as I have recounted in the division; and if you see it grow, then work on the patient's eye, and take a spatula slightly worn away according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the eyelash above subtly, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason approaches, then distill from your mouth to the eye a colic remedy made of litargyrum and red colic, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other treatment according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, as if an aposteme were hot, then let it cool down, and first cure the hot aposteme until it is healed; then begin the treatment again just as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts the eye by great harm, then suspend it with a needle and cut off part but not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill into the eye red colic made of litargyrum.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the prunele
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Es eyes of some men never have any redness, and cover the pimple and restrain upon the papers and turn away from the far end, and seem like a rose of balustrade; and the work is that the patient puts his head in thy hand, then thou workest on the eyes, and coil all that red stuff into suitable vessels for this, and sustain it with force; then cut the first layer, and go cutting right to the razor's edge until the end, and take care not to bleed the eye during the operation; and make the incision just as we have said in the incision of the ingrown toenail and with small forces when one removes the shell, just as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all red stuff removed, then use oil of sesame or you distill a red liquid like corrosive medicines, and put cotton on top of the eye with egg yolk so that it will be assuredly hot aposteme; and if there is nothing left, and the abscess swells up again, and thou dost doubt hot aposteme, then leave the eye and cure the aposteme with soothing things for hot aposteme; then return to thy operation until it is healthy, and thus do all the layers that are removed from the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you ease the cure of each weak oil by the natural way; and by the accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that those members are bearing up to that work.
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If there are veins that are red and covered on the eye, and they allow vision to work its job and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is then necessary for the first one that you look where the eye is, whether it is healthy or not, and there is no other disease except if the vein; then apply the bandage in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your shoulder, then suspend those veins up to the neck according to his wisdom, and let the bandages be fine and double according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two circles by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil those veins subtly with force, and remove the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins moving away from the eye; and beware that you do not touch the oil at the points of the spathous membranes, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut off those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the oil green and red pepper to corrupt what remains from the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to coil all of it in that hour, then apply a poultice on the eye with soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some days until the pains are eased and you are sure of an abscess hot; then resume in this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls this "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and by hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a reason in him that you incise on the abscess, where it should die, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then receive it with all the instruments by which this form is; and it is called "aspre chief", and be made of iron to one head again, and be pointed as a file so long as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this some times, then restore the surface with excitative medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is sealed, and flesh grows in it, and the bowels of the body are sealed, and remain thus for XL days, and it does not reopen and is not apostematized, and evil occurrences do not happen, know that he is healed; if not, then there is no other remedy than to return the fistula to its natural place according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with gentle medicines, and when it is uncovered so take a force according to this form, and let the iron be bent into three angles, and the point be thinned up to the tip as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, and esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os and le sent li malaides by that which the veins in it if he holds his hand on his cloth; and then restore the place of dry medicines such as I have taught you, and when the flesh has grown and hardened the parts, then the matter goes to the cloth; so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no obstruction to the nose or diminishment, it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal them, then apply poultices or bandages made of linen in a way that will not cause harm in order to draw out; then put on the eye a lien made from aloe, gall, and aloeswood, and then bind the eye with cloth and drapery; and the manner of the drapery is that you take soft drapery and double each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount the eye needs; then bind it tightly with a bandage and begin the poultices again in order not to cause harm; then remove the poultices and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the lien becomes moist, you should bind it very tightly; then remove the lien after a day and a night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, then repeat the application of the emplaister, drapery, lien, and poultices until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the tearing of the vitreous humor
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the vitreous humor, then it opens and comes forth like grains of resin, and it is shocking to see; then if you see it opening, the work is such that you insert an awl into the root of the part below up to where it is above, then insert another awl where there is a double thread from the part of the eyelid; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and bind a part of the vitreous humor around, and tighten it well, then extract the awl and put on the eye a wet linen cloth with egg white; and let it be until the threads choose with the vitreous humor, then cure the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the vitreous humor each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes from behind the eye and corrects the moisture of the albiginous and descends the eye, and enters as soon as possible; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eyebrow
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a boil that is assembled in the eye, resembling water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is this: you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take the head between your two hands, and lift it so that you see the boil come up to your eyes; then let it be fixed, and do not let it descend and be uncovered, and look at the patient's things as he would normally; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the boil's descent is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.
des aigues de l’oil	water of oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the likenesses of waters in division, and what is needed to pierce; so work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light by the sun, and his good eye should be stretched very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are to the left, or in your right hand if the eyes are to the right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are to the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are to the right; then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown, by the thickness of a hair, on that spot of the eye near the smaller tear-duct; then push the instrument called "almagda" properly, and turn your hand until it pierces into the spot of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the prune-leaf to the end of the nourishment; and that is the crown of the eye; if you see the bone on that paper by the clarity of the corneal fabric, then place the instrument just above where the water is, or press beneath one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little, and if the water rises again through the second route, put force with the instrument, and when it is well seated and does not move, gently extract the algumma in circling your hand piece by piece; and then put back into water a small part of the gemstone, and leave it thus in oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by dripping the oil into a cloth or a wet woolen rag in rose oil and abundant egg white, and mix with the pure oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now and those who are of our time, place a common broth with abundant egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too far in depth, but make it subtle, then put in the algumma as we have said; and upon the completion of the work, prepare for the patient's rest with the doctor present, so that he sleeps on his back in a darkened room; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be bound according to his disposition until three days; then release him in the same darkened house, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then put back the bandage until seven days; and it is not necessary that you do this during the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you hasten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Se apostemes chaus vient, that thou removest the oil before the seventh day, and direct it to that which allays aposteme; and when it is appeased, then remove the eye and set on its face a little hole to cover any day, and be there in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then come forth from the house step by step, and convert back to thyself; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the land of Yrach, who told us that in his country they made someone almagda pierce, so that they could suck up the water, but although I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read it in the books of the ancients; and by chance this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see; and they should be made properly from earthenware.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the ends of these should be of this same subtlety, and the last in three angled corners.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh to the neighbor
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes birthmarks or moles arise in various places, because of which there are some that seem like scorpions to many feet; and if there are such as have skin enchanted with fiery color, and others soft with bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then in that soft birthmark which is not enchanted, it is necessary that you cause the patient to sit between your hands towards the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour oil on those marks, and treat them warmly; then scrape with what you can sustain at the subtle edge of a razor on one side, until you know that that birthmark is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be pulled out, then open it with all one's subtlety and delicacy, so that nothing remains; and if without troubling oneself, or an aposteme comes forth, then cut as needed. And if they are malignant apostemes, then hasten and cauterize until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then pour wine onto the knee, and water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nail does not work, and moisture comes just to the palace, know that it is cured; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is bone near in the bone above, to which instruments do not come to cut: then you must put a linen thread about a finger thick, and be numb with your hands, and have between each night an interval of space or less; and place the patient's head on the thread at their nose power, and draw it into odorant so that it comes through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do this to children in schools, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the chief that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other chief that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know one after another in being as we are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Leave the flesh so long as you know the night has corrupted that part of it, then take the son, clean the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back on top just like before; do that for three days or more until all the flesh that remains is consumed by the ointment; and then put a cloth of cloth over some days until it is healed, and if it needs seeping medicines, use them; and that is the form of the instrument to purify the head, through which one distills oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or earthenware, resembling an open lamp, like a chain, and lead them also; and if you see, then make a closed chain, and have the instruments full to purge the chief; and have one handle on the chief to hold it when heating the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh to the neighbor
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there is a disease in the head of the neighbor which is called "tumor", and it grows and becomes large over time, so that it is visible to see; and therefore it is necessary that you make a hole at first, and remove all the fat, then put on top the fire cautery or burning medicine; and if one waits too long to do this until it is large, take heed if it is hard, of bad color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut it at all, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of gentle touch, not of bad color, and you can see that you can remove all of it, then empty the patient and the abscess without fear, and treat the wound with things soothing and restraining.
