quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neighbor is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knows that when a solution of continuation comes to one of these joint workings, it profits little, rather than in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to do what happens with anyone, if you look whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then join the two lips together with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of their flesh until they bleed, then assemble the two lips together with a suture, and tighten, and sprinkle powder over powder of dragon's blood, and incense broom; and put on the powders a piece of plaster or another plaster following, and leave it until it takes its course, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the seam is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some men have within their lips a hard abscess like grains of millet, smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut each notch, and take as pincers and cut in each part; then apply oil to the wound after the vitriolic incision, so that the blood is staunched; and then leave the wound open, and treat the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is flesh attached to the gums which the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let the bow or blood flow; then put on top of the wound vitriolic powder, or other powders restraining and desiccating; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs that are ugly and unpleasant; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as far as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth smell; it is necessary that you make the patient sit in your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs as they appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and yellowness and jaundice and other blemishes, until they are removed; and if one removes what is at the first stage, that is good; but if not, then begin again on the second day and third day, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, because those who use razors to clean between the teeth have different forms than those who use them to scrape off the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay the extraction as long as possible, because this should not happen at all; for it is a very high substance, so much so that one has no excuse for extracting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is forced to vomit, then you must be certain about the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	The patient suffers many times from the pain and thinks it is due to the tooth of Saint Denis, and has the good tooth drawn out; yet the pain does not depart by this means until the evil humour is purged, for we have already tried these methods with saints; and when you are well certain about the aching tooth, then you must scrape all around the tooth thoroughly to ward off the gum from all sides; then move it to your two or subtle pincers at the first notch and notch, until it is well loosened, then hold the pincers firmly; and the patient's jaw will be in your holy place between your knees, and you should hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump forth, then take one of these instruments and insert it into each side lightly, and move it just like you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, it's necessary to fill it with cloths, there where the perforations are; and if you strain it gently with forceps, so that it doesn't break from straining; and it's necessary to work very carefully around the gum for unseating the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take care not to break it, and leave a part of it, and the tooth will return to the patient through the wickedness of the root, causing him greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act as ignorant surgeons who, through their haste and boldness, break the cartilage and do not achieve what we have described; but sometimes bring great diseases through the roots that remain or through the cartilage they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the hole with vinegar or verbena and silk; and if blood comes out, which often happens, fill the hole with vitriol powder; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments with which one should extract teeth first are those with long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick handles so that they do not bend when pulling out, and be made of well-forged iron, and be toothed to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays at the trail, so it is necessary that you put on the site a moistened cotton ball in butter one day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the skin is softened, then put in forceps called "algefri", because it seems to have a beak of care; and be made inside as a file, that's its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of all these pincers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", which is also known as "palainche", for this reason:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be thick and large so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps over this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, for which the forms come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument that has two reins, for this reason:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fixings that are in front of the ratio of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like great pincers, for this reason:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break; and know that many instruments of the teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find for themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of cases, and one does not break the skin or the other bones, where it can, so he searches for instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, for this reason:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then replace it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural form of the body, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young girls, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly after the dentin, and is not in its right place, and one cannot smooth or file it: then draw a line; and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the form, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be made of iron with an edge in shape.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper becomes harder and harder in a few days because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a similar file of this form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little over a few days, so that it does not move until it is done; then make it smooth at the end to any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then file off the roughness as much as necessary, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loose, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without it falling out, and you have treated them with restraining medicines, but it does not work; so they must be restrained by a gold thread, because silver sons turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the width of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth shifting, take the thread and insert it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the gums between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering up to the part where you started, and restrain your hand subtly and slowly, until it does not move; and let your thread be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, and les assemble, and les repont entre le dent sain, and le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; and puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, and s'il deslie, or li filz ront, si l'estraint d'un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son temps, and c'est li forme des dens et li figure de l'adrecement des II dens sains, and des II meus, if tu vois:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then one puts it back in its place gradually, as we have said; and does not interfere with someone who is not wise and cautious, and at times one makes the form of a cow's bone tooth, and puts it in the place where there is a deficiency, and strains it so that it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None are the lines which come from under the tongue or by nature, as one is born thus; or by accident of a wound that has been sewn together; and the works are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your own hand, and lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous line of the large, so long as the tongue is disjoined from its seat, and if there is hardness or swelling, and this is due to a sudden wound, then put an unguent and cut the line of the large that binding; and take care that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, then lift up the patient's head with rose water and easy, or cold water, and then place a linen cloth under their tongue; and every night, wrap the patient in a cloth so that the wound cannot get worse.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bloodletting occurs, then place on the glass plate and let it flow; and if the blood flows forth, then cauterize with the slow fire cautery, which is good for this; then treat another treatment until he is cured.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see that it is of foul color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards gangrene, and there is moisture, then apply an unguent and make a fine poultice, and deliver it from one side to the other; and if the wound bleeds at your work, put vitriol on it until it is stopped, then return to your work as long as you are treating all the way; then raise the patient's head with vinegar and oil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there comes forth in the throat lumps which are called "godath", and they are properly known as "amandres"; and when you treat them, just as we said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard aposteme of little sense and dusky color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the bloodletting; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will divide it, or it would break apart by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to scrape, but first look to see if the aposteme is calm and appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Have the patient sit before the sun, and his feet be in good health, and have the work done on the mouth and have the servants hold the tongue between their hands, and press it down to all the instrument, by which this form is; and it should be of silver or subtle lead just as sharp knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue all along this instrument and you see the abscess, then take the needle and the thread in the almond, and draw it forward above as much as you can; and leave nothing loose with the threads, then cut off the instrument so that the form is like one force; and although the head is curved, and from one place to another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then cut off with forceps so that the form remains:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting from one part and the other part numb; and when you have cut off one of the almonds, then cut off the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and easy, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with vinegar, or grated pomegranate peels cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding ceases; then apply a cure until they are healed; and sometimes abscesses arise in the throat that are like the two almonds, so cut them off in the same way as the two almonds similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born inside her throat, namely the abscess of little sense; and I had well closed off all the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the obstructed passage, and could not eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had risen two fingers' breadth through the two holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and inserted an onion into one nostril, then the fire was applied, and a great portion of pus came out; then I refilled the other nostril with the onion and worked on the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the onion into that abscess, and cut off a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess recurred again and again, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I bandaged it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus she began to grow well; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to her after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the tumor rises to the eye and it is swollen and long, so it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below a great and rounded lump, so it is called "uvula".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, and you see that the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to cut it off; and that which is rounded and assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a fleshy color or black, then it is necessary to avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, to make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument which we have made a note of beforehand; then insert the onycha into the eye, and drive it downwards, and cut with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the superfluity that is beyond natural term; for if you cover more, you will grieve to voice and to word; and after incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear to cover, you should use artifice at the cauterization of the senses to calm their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is fine and smooth.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts their head on your shoulder, and then they press the tongue to the instrument which we have said in the chapter of cautery, and mix with fine living water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using this instrument, as shown by its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place your head or have someone else hold the medicine, as the hairs of a comb, and place the instrument on all the medicine above the vein; and have the patient sit up straight on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down to the throat and cause bleeding; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the vein, for the amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it turn white and the medication's irritations be appeased; and if you see fit, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument into all the cotton in the cane above, so that the cotton rises up onto the vein; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to start again with the medicine cautery, then restart it, and after the cautery, surround the vein with cotton wrapped in butter, and cleanse everything around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament, ysope, origanum, rue, camomille, and avronne, and similar herbs, and mix all or some of them together into one pot, and add a small amount of water, and make it boil; and let the pot be well glazed with earthy matter, and have an instrument inserted in the pot according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether of silver or of lead, and whether one of the key stones is inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is mortified; after which it often recurs, until the eye dries, and guard that you do not do this at the beginning of the swelling of the abscess hot, for many things happen there; and do not do this anything but at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and put inside the head a quill of egg, so that the mouth of the patient does not have too much heat; for the quill of egg does not allow the vapor to trouble the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it appears on the throat as a bone or fishbone, or nothing at all; therefore, you must treat what you can see, and press the tongue onto the sun at the instrument's entire length, so that you can see the thing being affected; and what does not become apparent and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit while the food is cooked in their stomach; perhaps this will dislodge the stuck thing through vomiting. Or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a dry crumb of bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then re-swallow it; and when it comes up again, you can pull out what we have said; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take an instrument made of plover according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu'il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;
de la sansue de la gorge	of the sweat of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for the sweat, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not benefit at all, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, then press his tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see pus, then extract it little by little with a small incision or with fine forceps that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, then take a woolen cord, and tie it around the patient's neck, then tie the hot iron to the cord and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is troubled by water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full vessel of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without choking, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the pus feels the water, it will spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit as we said, then suffumigate the patient with asafoetida at the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will eventually spit without difficulty.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and have the pos covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and in this perforation be the key of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient put the head of the pipe in their mouth, and shut the mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes just to the sweat; and the sweat will now fall, and if it does not fall, start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty things and such, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to pass through this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the sweat is such that when you can see it, it resembles curved pincers to enter the throat; and it has a resemblance to a doctor's beak, and has an asperity like lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and behold this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what is remembered here and there in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two manners in which one is like itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those who are at the core.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fatty part are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its judgment in work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if an abscess is not to be pierced until the bowels are full according to their completion; and if there are some that must be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, just as abscesses that occur near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints, and one leaves it until it is all rotten around it, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is on the main member, and if you delay perforation until it is all rotten, it will harm the main member; or it is at the foundation, so one should pierce it when it is ripe; and it does not matter that you do not pierce a ripe abscess without digestion being complete, except for the one that is at the foundation, which cannot be pierced deeply and becomes elongated inside, and thus forms an abscess; and it will not heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the sign of perforation of the abscess when it is dead according to completion, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the departures of fever are ended, and the reduction of pain and heat, and the quieting and soothing of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the perforation where it appears most prominent on the surface of the abscess, and where it opens up; and let the perforation be of sufficient length to reach through the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints, and on nerves and arteries, and in all equal parts where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who limp, due to pain in that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in its place and hardened, it's worth doing so that you leave the incision until it is confirmed in completed digestion as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you make the incision before that, the body will be drained of its venom from it, and it will be filled with much filth; and by chance the lips and the bottom parts will harden in it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, small openings; and in great abscesses, great openings, and many splits according to the resemblance of the greatness of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where one must cut off the skin, and cover; when it has become as worn out as a rag, and is exhausted, so you must do as with infants: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and if there are those whose covering is like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of angels; and if there are those where one makes a circular cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil who have not point of chief, if such aposteme souef superficial, it covient that thou loo perces plainnement; and covient when the apostemes is gros, and it has coillit grant bowe, and thou loo perces, if ne traire mie toute la bowe in that hour, but in train one part; then stope the aposteme just to another day, then in train no thing thereafter; do so by many times of good in good, until the bowe is out altogether; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or woman bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits tremble sometimes with the issue of the bowe, lest by chance the patient dies, and thou dost not take heed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your aposteme, if the wound is clean, and look to see if the wound of the aposteme is small; and if it's a plain cutting, then make tents of linen or old cotton; and if it's large apostemes, and there are many holes, then it's necessary that thou puttest in each one a tent so that they come together against one another; and if you have cut into the aposteme part of the skin, and you have covered it around, then it's necessary that you fill it with old cotton or rag of linen without moisture, and bind until the third day; then remove, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding during your work, so administer cold and clear water and moisten the cloth, and place it on the flowing blood repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, so administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is at the time of winter, and the boil or abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary to put on wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the boil is flesh-like, then it is necessary to put on wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine, until the third day, as we have said; and then release the abscess and discharge and cure it, as needed, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: and I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or the cure for head boils comes in small abscesses, and they are manners of ours that are in cloths, just as the yolk of an egg, and many have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	It is of fat and such where it has moisture also as pimples; and if there are such that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of tailing is such that you test all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes thus afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then make an incision above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, then scrape off without leaving anything the skin that contains that moisture, for it will return again if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound, and let it be until the next day; and those who are remaining from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reapply the cotton, just as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not linger overnight; then treat the wound with ointment according to what is necessary, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is not very large, cut it according to this form, from long; and remove the blisters, and scrape off all around, and put all your treatment of drawing out into a cloth where it lies; and if the artery makes you contrary, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with the abscess if it is pustular, and cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the pustular abscess and the moist one, if it is more light, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or the head does not have moisture, and I found this abscess just like a dry, rough, and white stone that could not be broken; and if one had done anything to it, one would have made as much a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, greater than those that come to the chief of children and roots of ears, the opening should always be at its most dependent place, so that the pus may issue; and the cure as it is needed.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck, and below the armpits, and also in groins, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and are very painful, and are swollen one against another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own coat, just as the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said; and similar things to these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Then when you see a good disposition to touch it, and it is similar in color to the body, and quiet on each side and not inflamed at the neck or artery or duct, and not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut above, and scrape off each part, and keep the two lips of the wound as close as possible, if you need to, just as we have said in abscesses of the head; and proceed slowly and carefully, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor should it be too tight nor too loose, so that your hand may escape, and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut off what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you open the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that stay blood, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it; and then examine your wound indicator to see if any small scrofulae remain, and cut them out.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a great vein at the root of the scrofula, then it's not necessary for you to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall away from there without harm; then apply the wound with old Egyptian cotton soaked in oil, and then treat.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you clean out the entire scrophula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, then there will be no excess remaining due to the greatness of the scrophula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and pull strongly, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that retain superfluity, open up where it appears more; and it opens in the same way as the one previously mentioned, depending on it, then tents with ointment and similar things are applied, so that what remains of the corruption is corrupted; and when the wound is well cleansed, then a cure with ointment brings forth flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of gangrene
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have gangrene, it is necessary that the incision of the throat which is called "epiglote" be avoided; and one does not provide help by doing so, because all the veins and the pulsations of the patient's body are hot in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both shoulders.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulsation, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, then, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four with a small opening in the middle, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the syphac; not in the cartilage; and these parts are suitable for the section of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all its extent, then cuts the leather until it comes to the knot; and avoids the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then closes the sycamore, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the fleshy part of the neck which springs forth through the broken place and due to the lack of voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the time is passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound by the key, and sew all smooth without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	All this said is that one should not do this just as long as the throat is completely filled, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the fault is being wasted.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglote because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut off part of the channels of the mouth; and I was summoned to cure her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and knew well that she had not cut open her jugular vein nor anything but the throat, and the blood was flowing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and cured her until she was healed; and it happened to the young woman that she lost her voice, and then returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of jasper, and it occurs mostly in women; and it happens according to two manners: natural and accidental; or natural ones have no artifice.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is according to two manners, of which one is similar to our fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and it should be feared, and one should not dare to do anything that might harm him who is small, and search every recess: if you find it like I did not think was fat, and cannot move in any way, then cut it off, just as one cuts through fat, and treat it with all your skill, if there is anything; and search well throughout, and cure it as needed, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	of the flesh
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many manners we are, all of which I will say resemble each other; and now it is necessary that I say the whole difference that is between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is hot and feverish, as long as the ebullition has not passed, and the corruption is accomplished; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nout there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains a sac called its own sac which is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a seed, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, either fat or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the flesh, that you prove and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "intermittents", according to what its form will come in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses in us is that you take or find the moistest part of the abscess and turn your two paws and paws, until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, according to the size of the abscess; then extract the foreign substance, and be careful so it does not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture pours forth quickly, regardless of its color, do it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision no more moisture comes, know that it is fat, so then do it in crosswise cuts, take it up with pincers, and gently scrape off each part and follow the direction where it lies, leading you to a healthy piece; and if you cannot lead it to health, then break it down into pieces such that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, then the wound comes back many times; and if there is only a little bit left, and the blood bothers you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, apply it to the wound, and put hot soothing poultices on the abscess, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the wound is large, then cut off two lips of the wound, and cure it with those who are familiar with skin.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or some other obstacle is contrary to your haste and you apply a leaden weight of vitriol, let it remain for two days or three, until the wound has purified, and the ebullition of blood subsides; then return to cutting what remains of the flesh.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here is the translation:
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of ulcers are many and similar, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and also ulcers that have two horns in three ways; and also ulcers that have three horns, and are in three ways; and also ulcers that have two horns, and single-horned ulcers, and are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these are cut, and some do not cut off more than from one side, which causes us to scrape the skin, so that we cannot tie the vein or nerve; and among these intervening things are the replies answered in bands, so that the patient does not perceive it at the opening of abscesses; and they come in three ways: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only on a charmed place, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a scraper for flax, according to this form, by which we stop blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that heals quickly from veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Breasts swell in some men when they begin to be corrupted, as much as they seem to be women's breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them must be treated according to this form from line .b. up to .g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and apply a medicinal paste to the wound by pouring in flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound at the seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast droops down and becomes wet due to its size as in women, then divide it into two sections above, with two similar incisions; so that one part holds onto the other at the end of each part, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from line .b. up to .g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about the seam and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed or the incision is not yet fully made because the patient does not want to rest or due to excessive bleeding, then you must fill the wound with damp cotton in corrosive oil; and leave it so that it dissolves the remaining fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are hard forms of scrofula or there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g:.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and care for it with ointment according to this form until he is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the kind like scrofula, then do it as we have said in incisions for scrofula, and if the wound discharges pus, then apply a cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.
