Et the manner of the work is that you command the patient to insert the intestine into their hand within the wound if it can be inserted; then be stationed on their collar between your hands and lift the flaps; then expose the cure above and cut all the skin of the testicles from the long; then put inside the leaves of the scale tied according to what you need to open the wound, so that the eye can issue; then scrape off the scab that is beneath the skin of the testicles until the white scab on top is uncovered from all parts; then insert your two fingers into the opening between the testicle and the white scab which is beneath the skin of the egg, and between the second scab, and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second scab; and then move your right hand within the cure of the testicles, and expose the white scab on top to your left hand, and lift the egg to all the scab towards the scale; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and release what is behind the bond; and take a needle where it has been made with 10 threads, and insert it into the back part of the scab which is after the skin of the testicles; then cut off the threads that appear on the other side of the threads, as many as there are four threads; then assemble one thread over another in the form of a cross, and tie the scab with a strong bond from two parts; then envelop the threads of the testicles and tie them strongly to two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter into them, lest an abscess arise; and put on top the bond according to the first long bond two fingers of it, and after these two bonds leave the scab which is beneath the skin of the testicles a great distance equal to one finger; then cut off in the part that is beneath the skin of the testicles as long as the flesh remains, and the bowels, just as we have said before; then apply wet linen to oil, and put it on wounds, and put on the bond that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white fatty tissue that we have said is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Because this happens many times, and let the bond be as long as it chooses for itself; and if it delays falling, then arise from hot water, and put what we have said on top of it until it falls; then treat the wound with another cure until it is completely well.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to do the treatment by fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made in the manner of the vine that surrounds the stalk, in such a way that you bind the vessels, after cutting above and below slightly; then cut into the middle, and treat the abscess of those who work, until the vessels fall; and cure it as we have said, until it is completely well.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	It never happens that a hernia comes out in the groin, as we have said, and opens up the swelling; and no intestine descends to the scrotum, and if it does descend, it's rare, and repair all hours; and yet if it stays too long in this position, the wound or syphac grows, until the intestine descends; and this happens through the stretching of the syphac which is in the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then becomes softened and swells the swelling and opens up; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes the cure is done with iron in this way: and it's that the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cut the swelling of the hernia which has swollen out from the wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphac which is under the skin next to the bone, then take the root and put it on top of the swelling appearing from the syphac; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut the two swellings appearing from the syphac on top of the root, and cut one and the other; then extract the top of the root, and do not cut the syphac or stretch the egg or any other thing, as I have shown you in the cure of the vine of the intestines; then cure it with the wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the sons, so mend and cure the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The groin is constricted, and has no appearance in the sprain, and the cauterization is more effective in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes soft in some men, because the things that are inside are softened, and it is a sight to behold; and when one wants to treat it, one must have the patient lie on his back, and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then tie the two edges together with a seam, and if you see fit, sew off the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is completely healed, and let the thread fall.
dou chastrement	The punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is provided for in our law, and therefore I would have been pleased if I did not speak of it at all in this book; and there is no need to mention it except by two manners: one being that the surgeon can respond when asked about a wound and its cure; and the other because we often have need to castrate certain beasts to help us, such as goats, sheep, and cattle and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: or by attraction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one where we do it by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then we take them in our hand, as long as they are released and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: instruct that you grease the animal, and press the skin of the testicles into your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut on each nut to the cop, when you have well scraped them; and leave any small or subtle scar tissue that is above the vassels; and this manner of chastisement is milder than that which is done by attraction, because at attraction something remains from the testicles, for which the animal desires lust; then heal the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	Of Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermofrodie is in two manners with men: one is that between the two testicles appears as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in court, urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is with women, and has on the thumb as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Et the cure of man and woman is that you treat the gathered wounds, and the wound itself as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the kidneys, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of Tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tenting is a gathered wound on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have as much as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should remove the excess of the tenting to your hand or fingernails, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deeply in, lest blood come forth, then treat another wound until it is healed; and one other sore that arises at the mouth of the hair, and the swelling, and by chance jumps forward, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and for this reason they called it "cow's disease" in ancient times.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you bind it, as we have said about the temperament, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of Erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is irregular if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or if the womb is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident by disease that has come; or it is caused by a hidden fault, or subtle or excessive humor, and it is done in front, in the sides, below, or wherever; and it hinders conception, and childbirth, and often gives rise to flowers having; and the knowledge of this is known through the sight of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swellings are nearby appearances, then apply them to the arms or the thigh.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is due to subtle humors and it appears near the two kidneys, then hurry, and do thus: place your two middle fingers together, and have the woman sit on her back, spreading her legs; then straighten out the two kidneys until the subtle humors are released, and cover the swellings; then take linen, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the area, and have the woman lie down at home each day, so that she cannot sweat.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sacrum is hard and dry, then you should lay on the spatula something like a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh birth, then suspend it at the incision and lay on the spatula; and have medicines that stay blood, such as aconite, dragon's blood, incense, together with much egg; then administer a cloth of linen wide, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus be long enough, then provide a tent of dry linen; then cure other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes flesh birth, then it should be covered according to this manner, unless it is incurable abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an incurable abscess that is in the marrow, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Of Hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Varices are openings of veins that do not have a natural opening, and when varices are old they become ulcers; and we have said in the division those who resemble them, and their signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are deeply embedded in the rectum, and do not appear to sense, except by iron remedy.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the rectum, where one can feel them, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then extinguish the pile with forceps, and cut it at its roots, then powder on restraining blood medicines such as aloes and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet to the ankle for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if any bleeding comes forth, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he stays, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him take poultices to the back and breast so as not to hurt; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of elder with old wine, and apply to the wound.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess heals, so treat the wound with oil until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so cover it as I said to do the same; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Of Abscesses of the Womb
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the mother, such as chance and stony abscess and herpetic abscesses and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the womb, which is not one of the abscesses that boil forth; and if you want to know how to work with iron, then look to see if the abscess is inflamed at its beginning, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the patient recover until the pain is alleviated; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have two small stools or he leans against them, and support him on his back and assemble his legs away from the leg; and be his hips spread, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then succeed to the left side of the right shoulder, and install the instrument with which one works the mouth of the womb, of which the form follows; and it is necessary that when you see fit to install this instrument, that you place the first notch in by to know the depth of the womb, so that what enters into the instrument does not come more than a finger's breadth deeper than it should, and that it does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depths of the womb with cloths, so that the instrument does not annoy him; and it is necessary that he put the horn of the instrument above, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et when the abscess opens and one makes it soft with the hand, then it is necessary to cover it at the head, at the shoulder joint; and when the bowels are empty, then it is necessary that you put in the wound damp cloths soaked in rose oil or green oil; and place the cloth far from the wound at the bottom of the marsh, and put a cloth above the marsh and above the pointed linen cloth netted with water or mallow cooked; then cure after two days of anointing as needed until it is healed; and sometimes remove the bandage and the wound by pouring water and honey, and then water or roots of lilies and long Aristolochia are cooked; then return to anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is stuck in the marsh, then it is necessary that you take care not to cook with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and signs that are when you see the woman hasten downward, and desire to give birth: then the child hastens forth quickly; therefore know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue comes under his head, and the secondine with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on her belly so that the child comes out soon; for when he descends above his head, then the secondine is with him, and the marriage is freed from its superfluities through good purging; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens sometimes under its feet, and comes forth the body or the head, or hands, or when it comes under his belly, or shoulder, and is converted by chance above his neck, and through other bad figures; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out above its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her virtues are weak, then make her sit on a stool or have women hold her; and let the mixture of oil or fenugreek be cooked, and then pour it between her breasts, a little spatula-shaped thing, which is in this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	et fende la secondine, and cut the afterbirth, and cope a son ungle until the moistors which are in there flow; and take the belly of the woman until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to purge the woman with fenugreek decoction with sesame oil; then make her take and estrue of condisi, and keep her mouth and nose one hour: so now the child will.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, then it is necessary that you pull them back gently piece by piece; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then take away the stool from the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall down; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the blade that was put there before, and extract the child, and pull back equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, it is necessary to support it high up; and then turn it little by little until it is even; then take hold of its feet and stretch them out little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump up to the crotch, if it is commanded to, and make it stutter with conditions; if it jumps further, God will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not further as we have said, then turn it a little at a time, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take mugwort from aloes, and oil of sassafras, and boiled gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of a woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in lukewarm water up to the navel; and when she is moistened underneath, then apply a collar of myrrh, and place it underneath, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her strain her mouth and nose, and press lightly on the belly, for the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From childbirth on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, so it puts its hands on and off; then it looks up at his neck, and the feet hang down below, and it leans forward over the bed; and folds its hands on and off, and then takes hold of its hands on the belly, and removes the cushions underneath, until it is prepared to come down; and if the child does not jump, so takes its feet and moves them forth, then moves the belly up, then puts its hands in; and rocks the child on and off; and commands the woman to take hold as long as the child comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From childbirth when the child comes with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, so make the woman get up and go; if she cannot go, so make her lie down on the bed, and take away her legs forth; then administer the oiling that I have described; and if she does not give birth, so make her sit on the stool, then study how to bring back the hand; and rock the child according to its natural shape, and let it be quieted, and command her to take hold as long as the child comes forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From childbirth on its neck, with spread-out hands and face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the ball holds its hand, then turns it little by little and lightly; and when it is even, so puts on the natural muscular power of aloes and oil, as we have said, then instructs it to move little by little; and when you have done this, so makes it sit on the siege, and instructs it to take hold; and makes it stretch out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way to all the swelling, so cut the swelling at the fingernail, until the moisture is emptied; and if the child pours onto its face and neck, then cut it from the mouth, so that it is not retained, and kill the child; then put the child inside, as much as you should, and instruct the woman to take hold sometimes: then let it come out lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	From childbirth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live at all, unless they are named; I know this, that they multiply and are separated by the sow's itch that divides them, which is tied to the skin; and sometimes they come out as naturally as others do, so we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out quickly, as the treatment we have said, and the bail is subtle, and does what it does soon and lightly; and does so that it moves towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of an infant by the measurement of divine glory, and it is necessary that the bail knows everything, because similar things happen by chance; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman after giving birth to a stillborn or dead child, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to perform manual work; then you must know if the woman is of good health, and has no accident or fears death; then the woman should be positioned on her back, with her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister will give her a poultice of two parts, where she lies in bed so that she is not disturbed by the descent of the child; then anoint the mouth of the mother with moist oils mixed with althea and fenugrec and flaxseed, then grease the baby's hands with these oils and those unguents; then pour them into the mother lightly, then take heed if the child appears to be descending onto its head; then place the onychas in her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or below the beard or under the chin or near the ribs, and if the descent is over the feet, then place or pin it to the sides of the body; and you must hold the onychas in your right hand, put the corset between your left hand's fingers, and pour all over your left hand lightly, and place the onychas in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to an empty thing; and this is the form of the onychas:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Afterward, place it opposite another one, or the third if you have need of it, so that the extractions are equal; and then stretch it equally by moving from one side to the other, in order for it to come out, and let the needles hold it in place, just as this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part, then anoint the ball with some of its own oil and put it in that part, and stretch the other part; and if none remains, then place this needle or more higher up, and do this until everything comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back because of the constriction, then you must wrap it with a cloth so that everything comes out; then cut into the joint of the sole or at the heel, and thus you must do to the other hand, and also with both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu peux; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the extraction is gentle, and the direction to the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	Et s'il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l'estraies à l'enveloppe it sur la main; et fend le ventre ou le pis, tant que les moix qui i est corré; et si les autres membres sont osteit, et le chiez demoure, si bouche la baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusque à la bouche de la marris; puis i bouche l'once ou II, et le traie plus loin; et si la bouche de la marris est rétrécie pour apostème chaud qui i est venu, si n'y covient mie travailler, ains covient aménistrer choses moites et grasses; et l'aménistre emplastrés, et siece en eau mollifique et amoistante.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on his side and you can put him equal, so treat as we have said for a living child; and if one cannot, then treat it by parts, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the abscesses that we said come to the marriage; and if bleeding comes forth, it should be restrained with water, and other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly contained a dead child, then she consulted with another on top of it, and rejected the death of the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her mouth, and swelled up so much that it opened, and began to cause great perturbation.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on an emplaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days, another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly does not have bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wished to heal the wound, and in removing bones, as long as the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived for a long time thus, and sometimes took a little rest from that place; and I do not recall this chapter well except for this, that when the master finds an unusual thing, he should know how to intervene.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	and bring back the mother to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Next comes the shape of the pressure, with which one reads the books; and to the two turnings at the two joints of the two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the corners should be more subtle than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the fist should be two palms wide, and the margin of the trees one palm and a half; and between the two hinges there should be two adjustments of this same fist, which are fastened on both sides by half a palm in length or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marriage to open when turning the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	One other form, made more subtly and lightly like it, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of pliers; and have two joints, just as you see, one palm long and two broad; and when you open the mouth with all the instrument, so set the woman on the bed, her feet apart and legs spread, then put the two joints together in the mouth and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips; then work your hand with all the instrument, just as you have made the pliers equal, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the marris, until the woman makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and their similarities multiplied; and when the apothecaries have prepared them, then is the work more hasty and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	So do not despise the instrument that you have prepared, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then make her blow softly with conditi, and hold your hands at the mouth and nose; and if she starts to cough because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, I take the pot, and make a pit or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the maris, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, cassialigne, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or boiled in water on the fire; then put a cord or pit from the pot, and the other head into the mouth of the maris, and tie it so that the vapors come inside the maris; then make it vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the afterbirth comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not fully cured, instruct the patient to wet her left hand in sesame oil or muscilage from althea, and then put it in its natural state, and want the secondine; and when she has found it, take it and stretch it a little bit directly, so that the maris does not resist extraction; but it is necessary to move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull it out; and it will come out and settle.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	Et if the mouth of the womb is narrowed, we have said the treatment to be loosening and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not as all that we have said, then take care not to proceed further; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the womb, you tie to the navel of the woman, then anoint her with quadruple medication ointment; so she will be helped and restored, and will come forth; but still, when she has given birth, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to do fumigations suitable for this: none of the ancients have proved the fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it appears like a dog's chain, and one puts the head in a subtle natural way, and wide shoulders above the fire; and let there be fumigations over the coals, and comb it until it is worn out, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fontanelle pierced, but it is stopped by a subtle membrane: therefore it is necessary at the bath that she pierces that membrane with her own hand, and does not touch the surrounding area too much, and secure the bandage so it is not touched; then put a wet cloth on vinegar and oil, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put in a hole a cord of cloth, and let it stay for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from sudden wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that stoppage: if it is cured, as we have said of the cloth cord.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules which come from under the fundament are nodation, and grow greater than those which come from above the fundament to depart, or in the space of II parts, whether one fistula or more; and when that nodation is ancient, it works, and brings forth moisture, either white or subtle, and sometimes these fistulas perish; and they are known by this, that there is evacuation, or egestion, or ventosity when the patient makes egestion, and by chance one bursts forth.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and reach just to the joint of the crotch, and just not to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula is perishing at the fundament, or not perishing: and it is that you insert your index finger or fundament into the fistula, and push a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twistiness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twistiness, then I push a thin tent or horsehair into the fistula, as far as you feel the tent or hair at your fingertip; and if you don't feel it, and there is no evacuation, nor ventosity, nor discharge, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; therefore hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends all the way to the bladder or the urinary channel, and it lets out urine, and cannot be healed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just to the joint of the hip, then the tendons are coming just to the place; if there is no twisting and the invention of pain around, then it stays thus bent, and there is no value in medicine or ointment by rubbing; and in these pus-filled ulcers there is no cure other than hard labor, and the vanity of foolish doctors who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not pus-filled and not old, there is hope of recovery by iron, as I have experienced, and the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips sloping towards his belly; then spread a linen cloth or a plack if there is twisting, until you know where the tendon comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should place your two fingers there, if he senses at once that the tendon has been pierced; and be discovered where you feel between your thumb and finger or flesh, then you know she is pus-filled; if not treated at all one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	On dist toutefois que l'on peut bien guérir quelques-uns, mais cela arrive rarement; et l'aide que l'on y fait, si est que l'on échauffe le cautère subtil selon la largeur de la fistule, comme il est devant dit; et le bouton tout chaud dans la fistule, tant qu'il vienne au-dessous du fondement; et fais-le deux fois ou trois fois, jusqu'à ce que tu saches que ces charres fautues soient brûlées, qui sont semblables à une plume d'oiseau; et puis le cure d'oignement enlevant char et soudant.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If so, otherwise he cannot be healed; and if the tent intervenes, and does not pierce all the way to the foundation that is at the bottom, and between your thumb and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or syphac, and you see the fistula in the direction of the covering of skin; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the tent, and then apply the cautery after, until it reaches the top of the tent; and the tent will be delivered, and will fall; then remove those charred remains that resemble a bird's feather, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood swells up and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Car the cauteries of fire assemble two things: that is to say, the burning of those joined bones, and the cessation of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of damp tents in butter or in broken cheese, until the pus flows out, and then the charred bone is issued into the pus; then cure the wound of ointments flowing from hard skin, and are the dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the fundament and is far from the body, then insert your two fingers into the fundament and investigate this matter.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you sense the tent, and between two is the cloth or the sponge or bone, where it is about to pierce, unless there are fires that go only by way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of three manners: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you scrape down to the foundation, or if you can put tents and cure it as first; and do not go too deep into the parfont, lest you cover the tenement which holds the foundation, and cause the egestions by way of unwillingness; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and then mind the bone that is faulty in the wound, as long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: if it were a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes blisters are formed in this manner: and it is when you burst the tent in the blister, and it is on the side of the foundation beneath the skin above, so take a pierced tent at the top according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I insert one twisted thread into two, and insert the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then take out the thread from that perforation, so that you burst your dough or foundation; and treat the top of the thread, and assemble the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and let it stay for a day or two; and sometimes restrain it, until the filaments that are between the two break loose and fall out; then cure the wound until it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not puncture, then make it puncture in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not need to be cut so far down and then cured, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spinal thorn from which one makes a blister is very rough on one side and notched; but on the other side, it is not, because that's why you don't break what you shouldn't break, as you see here.
des emorroydes	of wounds
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes are according to two manners: or they are within the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and great ones, and in court there is blood, and there is one or more, and they come out from the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture, and in court there is a little yellow water or a little blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them within the foundation is that you instruct the patient to stretch so as to come out in chambers, until the foundations come forth, and the sons are seen; then hasten, and hold it with pincers, or grasp it at your finger, then cut at its roots; and if the linen cannot hold due to its moistures, take it by the napkin, or by a piece of cotton; and extract it to your hands, then cut, and powder on some hot powders that are in place for cauterization; or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter on cauterization, then cure other cures until they are clean; and if the foundations cannot come forth, instruct the patient to take a sharp purgative drink and bitter to cleanse what is within the foundation, so that it may come out openly; when the patient takes fright, and the sons have come out of the foundation, then the cure is light; and it is that you grasp it at your finger or with pincers, cut, then cure as we have said, until they are clean, and fear cutting by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit du large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noie le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I pour corriger la superfluité du sang; puis met sus le fondement drapeil moilliet en oile rosset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et commande au malaide qu’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cessés, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sainz.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the putrefaction of the devil or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is putrefaction of devils in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you treat a boil or a toenail with the bark on top which does not allow it to moisten; then treat it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot dry, start the scraping again stronger than before, until it heals outwardly; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Furuncle is a small abscess appearing outside the body and goes very deep; and never will it freeze, and one feels it as much dead from tremor, and comes to all the body, and more in the arms than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a cord made from an ostrich feather or a strong vulture feather, and place that cord on the abscess, until it girdles the abscess all around; then turn your hand so that the cord goes all around the abscess, and put it deep inside, and pull out the abscess from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, then do so with a cord of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and above, drawing it up.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	but do not pierce, in order to keep it at the two, and press down. And if you see fit, then cauterize the tremor, as is said before or in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of purgation
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a purge of silver or archaute, or melted iron or cloth; and sometimes one makes these small and large instruments, according to the way they are brought together.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then which are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of purgation, small and great, is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it has a fissure where the belly is bound, as you see, and the head is pierced within; and it has two perforations on one side and one on the other; and the belly or womb should be covered with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around by small perforations, and there should be one space between each perforation, then pour into these perforations one thread of strong silk twisted ten times around, and assemble the belly as if it were a she-goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread in front, then poultice; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the poultice with oil or almond oil from a hen's egg, or something similar, then tie it lightly; then press on the minister with both hands together until he is completely covered, then remove the poultice, and lift the patient's legs to the ceiling, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it be as long as it can; and if he sleeps one entire night, it will be a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purify him in a disease of rectal obstruction, and the medicine hastens to come out, then rebegin it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, so be the cysts also subtle as for a child; and it is the form of the subtle cyst above which the skin will be strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and from what things they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the hitting of stone, and cutting with sword and knife or lance or pole or arrow or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from hitting with stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you fear hot abscess: then make it heal as quickly as possible with cephalic remedies, especially if there's pus coming out of the wound, and let it heal on the opposite side of the injured part; and make the patient replenish with wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not wish to be healed, then let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put a poultice on the wound, if there is an abscess that comes, with a cloth moistened in rose oil or in vinegar; and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound, if it is fresh to its very blood, and has not been moved by air, as I will say more about this later; and if the skin has been moved, then put some ointments on, until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the cut of a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together with suturing, just as I will say for belly wounds from suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and gapes, and holds only by a little, then scrape it off; next, treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of soft skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like poults, and similar things.
