Unhealed wounds are not applied to except in members where one cannot put poultices because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare bones, such as those of the hand or neck, and others similar; and the quality of the user is that when you find wounds that are in sweet and clean water without bruising, then take them; and put one in a sweet water bath, until they become familiar and have nothing in their bellies; and then be cured with wine and poultice, then rub the member so much it becomes red, and put on the unhealed wounds; and when they are full and swelling, if it is a place where one can put a poultice, then put it, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the limb easily and then with water, very well, and then bind it; and if the bandages are too tight around the body, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is much increased, apply powdered vitriol or gallstones and similar things until it subsides; or you put half a handful of peeled fava beans on the limb, and leave them there until they are absorbed by the limb, and then it will subside; and if you need more, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bandages do not want to take hold, rub the limb with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the swelling goes down, and then apply them; and as soon as they feel the blood, they will be absorbed; and when you see that they are dripping, powder on top a little bit of alum and silk broom, or ash, so they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a treatment for fracture and desolation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish doctor falls from this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books nor read letters; and because of this reason is the science strange in our land, for I have never found good one; and I know nothing except by the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have reduced the science to writing, and through experiment, and through the habituation of my life; and I have described what is contained here in this chapter, and abridged it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are prepared, just as I did in these two chapters beforehand.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we say the prologue to this book, which contains the summaries of words and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breaking or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, you should hasten to heal the patient on both sides, unless something hinders it, such as weakness of the body, or youth, or old age; or if the time is not too cold or too hot; and beware of cold fevers, that is to say, chills, and flesh of goat and hare, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty foods, and do not fill oneself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about a hot aposteme, or an expansion of matter in the member; then let the patient return to their previous governance as they are used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or if they have viscosity, such as boiled wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and peas, and pork belly, and eel, and fresh fish, and rich wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with great nourishment the bones are restored more quickly and the fracture is healed sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature pour la sechor des membres ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre si com os de petis enfans; mais n'a cure ramoinne sus l'os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s'aert et joint le membre ensamble tant qu'il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre et pour ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes si com nos avons dit.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is one thing and the fracture of the belly or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur by being struck, and others by being crushed, such as the cutting of a feather to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And then there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture in a small split or crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And at every manner has its own device and proper instrument in restoration, according to what the memory comes into place; and it is known that the break of the bone by what the joint is twisted, and appears well by deficiency, and sounds under the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twistiness or sound to touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no break; but it can have twistiness, or a crack, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you must not move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come next, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Et saiches que the breakage that goes in arvol, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary to put them back into place equally, so that abscesses do not arise; and if abscesses come, let it stay for a day or more, until the abscess is appeased; then put it back into place as you can easily and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of one where there are pieces; then strain it, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, and you need to straighten two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or at your hand it is small members, or at two tendons, or one tendon and at your hand; and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, then reunite by all means the additions in their places as you can, and take care that through your work the patient does not suffer injury or pain; and align well the two joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well: so straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press it as those who cause by their work abscessed heat and contraction in the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, thus chastise well the patient that he not move it, nor while watching nor sleeping, nor turning nor in any other way; and take care that the member be so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and it is necessary to put him in such a condition that he does not feel any pain; and take care that he be set straight, so that there are no twists when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken member are as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: thus it is necessary to wrap them in soft and subtle linen drapes; and for those that are large, such as thighs and calves: thus it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and strong bandage, because the wide bands encircle all the great member and hold it equally tight from all sides, so that there is no crease; then tie around lightest stitches, three or four according to the member, and strain your hand slightly on each band, then go up to the break and strain less, so that the break will move away a bit; and soften the band slightly and slightly, until you take a great part of the healthy flesh, then take another band and wrap around again from above over the broken limb; then go down to the part below the break and hold it moderately, not too tight nor too loosely, as we said in the first lesson above; then put linen or drapes between the bands, until they are all even, then tie everything up with a ribbon, and then put well-made stays on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or swelling, he sets something calming on top of the abscess hot and which takes away the swelling, and leaves it like that for some days; then strain onto those stars, and let them be half a width of a large cane, or of fir wood from which one makes clefts, or of palm tree sap, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the star you put on top of the break be a little bit bigger and wider than the others; and let it be as long as it needs to be for the limb of small or great size; then strain onto the stars just as you did at the first stage, then tie above with a thread in good order, just like at the first stage on top of the break; tighter it is above, sooner it will be less so; and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; for if the thread is thick, as I have seen with the works of foolish people who make their own strings from twisted flaxen cord, and that is a great error, for the string cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not necessary that there be less than two fingers' width between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after the straining in their healthy parts, then put under them cloths of linen or felted wool, so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage, and the ligaments are broken, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set splints on all the broken members the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Car when the members are great, there is no need to put them in place more than after three days or seven, or more according to your security about what happens happening; and behold here the manner of ancient ointments to restore breakage, dislocation, and twisting: and it is that you take wheat flour that remains on the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the ointment restoring breakage in many dispositions, and especially for women and young children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting: take aloes and ladani and inula and assefeitide and gum arabic and mugat, each 10; myrrh and aloe, each 5; alechil 8; and make powder, and mix it with many eggs; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is worth for twisting: take mugwort and marjoram, anise seeds X parts; myrrh and aloes, IX parts; dragon's blood VI parts; Armenian balm X parts, and grind well, and mix with water or an abundance of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and bones out of their places, and to soothe the pain occurring, and use the bone, and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in ale and cooked oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not heal entirely, but they are good for soothing a hot abscess and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig tree and leaves of terrestrial papyrus, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to ease the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, vetch flour, each in equal parts; and pound, and mix with wine, and apply to the members if they are heated, or mix with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Pren racines of vismalve, and seed of flax, balaust, mellilote, and sansuce, and flowers of violets and camomile, from each one part; and grind, and mix with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore it with a cerot made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member to restore it with things dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster that is good for a lesion and pain: take mugwort and horsehair of sheared men or bird feathers, and vervain, in equal parts, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not loosened by hands days. If pain comes to the place, or pruritus, without rest or swelling, then hasten, and loosen it, and remove the emplastrum now; and take a light cloth, and a moist sponge from the sea, and plunge into water, and lift up the place, until the pruritus ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, damp in water or rose oil, and bind with a nut, as long as you are sure of no hot aposteme; and repose the inflammation of the member, and may the pain be gone, then recommence the subtle binding, and a little emplastrum, and do not strain it so hard as before; and subtilize until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is gone and red and painful and swollen are all removed from it, and you need to plaster and bind, then start again in the same way as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Et s'il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s'aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j'ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n'est, saiches que norrissemens n'i puet venir; arose lou donques d'aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c'est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n'i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l'ovrer droitement.
des diverses manieres de brisure	The various ways of breaking [injuries]
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of breakages are, and various figures, and the causes are destined; for there are breakages that are made by percussion of a sword, and the collarbone is stripped bare to the socket which is below the bone, just as a hatchet or axe does; and therefore this type of breakage is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing, and is called this kind of breakage "absolute"; and the wound from these two breakages is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is an embedded percussion, or a splitting, or a blow from the fist of stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a persistent breakage which approaches just to the membrane that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is glued to the bone as subtly as a mouse, and it is a small fissure, and therefore this breakage is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by piercing with an arrow, or by falling, or by similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter downwards, and the bone is shaved like blacksmiths do when they hammer on furnaces; then the arrow goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones, like the head of an infant; and it happens to all these types of breakages where small pieces are dislodged as they are; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of breakages by their subtraction above them, and the inquiry into their tents, and through the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it gently above, then opens up the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the breakage, take care to note the accidents of the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of blood, loss of intellect, swelling, palpitation, fever ague, and the flesh issuing forth and turning red, and other similar things in many dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unbearable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the 14th day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the membrane below the bone is corrupted, and come the accidents that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	Et if the break in the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut through the broken part thus: and this means that you take hold of the patient's head wounded, and uncover above the bone in all the ways you can, and above the shape of the wound as gentle as you can, and if bleeding comes out to reveal the bone, or an abscess forms, then the aid of what is needed comes; and this means that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil; and make the wound rest until the abscess is appeased, and be assured of no further bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is to cut straight ahead, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another shape larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have diverse shapes, some being narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of untempered iron; and work lightly, lest you wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and rough, then you must pierce around it, so that you give shapes with rasps, not too deep lest they go beyond the bone of the skull, and it should have above the point a margin or one circle, so that the point does not go beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each becomes its place in the shape of the bone, so that you have rasps for all tests; and this is the form of the three manners of rasps:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one rasp on the bone and turn it in your hands until you know the bone has been pierced; then place the rasp elsewhere a little further, and do this all around, then file away the incisors of the bone which is between the ridges, and make it more subtly than you can, lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand or to one of your tools like pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you remove the fragments that remain of the bone to all other instruments resembling a chisel, but it must be more sharp and subtler than the other chisels; and if there remains nothing of the small bones or no scales, then gently extract them with the same instruments; then cure the wound by using tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which the Gauls say, which is more sound; and they love it very much, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lenticular incisor, and this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut off at one end, and the parts are aligned in two directions, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly chop around the entire bone, and take good care to guard the skin that is below; if it becomes attached to the bone, gently lift it, for one lifts well without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is filed away only on top, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to remove scales with a subtle scraper which you should have in various quantities, so as to administer in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So start with large scrapers, and then move on to more subtle ones, and do not stop until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-like and subtle breakages, it is necessary that you administer according to its direction; and this is something that is not known to him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is open, it is necessary that you take one cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this as gently as possible so that you do not harm the abscess, then administer above the other layer, and do not strain it too much except until it keeps the wound alone; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the swelling is pacified, then release it, and administer medicines such as roots of linden, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make powder of these things, and place it on the wound, and administer again without application of ointment; and beware that the wound is soon clean, lest you leave off anointing, nor let the edges assemble, for when the edges assemble above the skin of the head, they flow and burst forth, and great harm comes to the patient; for when one puts something biting on the abscess, it bursts open above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take care then, if any bad accidents befall the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no other remedy that comes from the medicine we have applied on it, which has such virtue, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix one drachm with it; then apply it to the spot where the boil is; then treat it in the ways of cures that are necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the neck above are broken, or one on its own, because these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must take your little finger or a small reed, and put that break inside your finger's nail, and straighten it slowly, until the nail returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the neck and cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it equal at the head of a rod slightly large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then do it again, and hasten to restore the first part, if you can; if not, after seven or ten days, when the abscess has cooled down, then straighten the tip of the nail with a linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put another on the other side, if there is a break there; and let the tents be so large that they fill the perturbations of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said some physicians that one must moisten the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that it is good, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a mixture of egg white and flour powder; then leave the tent, until the bone is hard and the ligaments are tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one places a bottle or eggshell instead of tents, and if it has a single soft draping around, and holds the breeze, and blows on the patient among them; or does what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess forms nearby while you are working there, then put a poultice or damp cotton cloth in oil of rosins, or in one pot of aquilone.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come, so apply an emplaster by default, with barley flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white; then put on gentle steam, and do not bind the night; and if the break in the night is small, and it is broken into small pieces, so stretch to suitable instruments for this, then sew the tear, and cure things in a natural way, binding and healing, as emplasters and ointments are suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the night, so treat the tent, and put weights of cloth on it, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below, and there is no wound outside, and the break is just so, and is not split in two, only that it is known slightly inside, one recognizes it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part of the jawbone, that you put your two index fingers in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is in the left side of the mandible, then put your two index fingers from the right hand, and press the break slightly inside, and bind it with equal force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split in two, then it is necessary that you administer an extension of three parts, until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or fracture, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a poultice on the broken jawbone, and put a double drapery on it; and put a great iron plate, well made, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and bind it as tight as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and give him light victuals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape is changing, then loosen it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and put a poultice on it, of mill powder with egg white or barley meal, after you have removed the previous poultice; and put a light woolen cloth on top, and if the poultices harden, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it so until he is healed; many times he is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess forms, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, take care that no part of the bone is left; if subtlety to extract with suitable instruments for that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, then sew the wound if it is large, and put suitable poultices on top to bring forth flesh, until he is healed.
de la forcele	of the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture is broken multiple times in front of the shoulder, and the break is such that it is divided into three manners: or it is broken and split in two, with pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the break has no wound that you have two assistants, so one holds the assistant's tool that feels the fractured forcele; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put the break in your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, then place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded spear of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your need; and strain and lift the forcele, and hold the spear in your hand, so that you put the break in its proper position.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forcele forward because it comes from behind, then it is necessary that the patient lies sovining on his hatedil, and puts a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder; and instructs the assistants to bring down the shoulder, until the bone of the forcele is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find it disjointed, then it is necessary that you split it open; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, then file it with one of the incisors that you have; but put this instrument under the forcele to protect the sac.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems like a spoon, and is not shaved, and be as wide as it should be, according to the greatness of the bone and the power of the work; and have two joints, just as you see, and one large and the other narrow, just as the rifting of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, so count the wound, and if the rifting is small, or you doubt of a hot abscess, then apply the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, then soak a cloth in oil of rosins, and vinegar, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without trimming, is that you put on the bone a plaster made from mill powder and egg white, and put light bandages on top, and place a small spear under the armpit if needed; then take a very wide bandage of one palm's width, then put a double cloth over the bandages and the plaster; then take a thin strip three inches long and wrap it around that bandage so that the chief of the bandage are hanging; and place the strip on the breakage, and turn the bandage around the neck and under the armpit healthy and unhealthy; and gently remove each part, and when you see that the binding is holding the breakage properly, and you clearly see that the strip is not moving over the broken bone, then reward each day, and when the ligaments loosen, then restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit so that he can lift the aid in high; thus ease the breakage of the shoulder by aligning the shoulder joint, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not untie unless bad accidents come, for up to 20 days; then reapply the plaster if you see that it is needed, and strain and leave it so, until he is restored; and he is restored in at most 28 days, and less than that with some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Poc avient que li espaule brise or large leu ne em mileu, and ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l'apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, and la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, in toutes les manieres that tu peux; puis met sur le leu poudre dou molin with abun d'uef, and estoupes legieres, and met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus una estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l'espaule, and se desoz l'estele est chevemens in any leu of l'espaule, si emple celle cheveure d'estoupes de lin, si that li estele siece igalment; and puis l'estraint a tout una grant bende fermement, si that li estele ne se mueve de son leu, and regarde le liien chescun jor; and toutes les fois k'il amolist, si l'estraint, and met igal l'estele s'elle est fuer de son leu, and gise li malaides sus son costeit; and li espaule est restouree in XX jours or en xxv. Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, and soies seur, car ce n'est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes before and points under the skin, then fill it with, and remove the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the humerus to calm down an inflamed abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the rib
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is sometimes broken in middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in middle, then it sinks below, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks sustenance, and altogether, and by chance bleeds blood, and opens up the sinews in the broken bone, and feels well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient sits up on his back, and puts 1 cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and makes it even in all ways you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put emplaustres and bandages above the subtle bandage of salt, or another light one, and wraps it in 1 cloth, and ties it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the binding back around to the back, and bind it gently, and reward each hour by loosening, and if it swells again, bind it again; and if it is necessary to unbind due to corrosion or pruritus that comes at the joint, or pain or abscess, then hasten and unbind, and remove the emplaustre, and address what has come forth in ways of cures; then reset the emplaustre, and bind it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not come forth except in thick places after the back, and at the top inside, and do not bend forth except because they are slippery; and one senses it well by probing the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you put it equal to the break, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the poultice, and bind with a bandage, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels extremely great pain and piercing, as if from pleurisy, for the bone pierces the skin; and breathes with difficulty, and all, and vomits a great amount of blood, and this is grievous sickness, and the ancients have placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly to push the breakage away from the inside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless an inflamed abscess has come before it.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should put poultices on the joint to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the poultice might attract unnecessary substances to the joint due to the condition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the joint with moist wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the breath around, then take care of the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear through the bone which points to the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken ribcage, and it is necessary to put something underneath the instrument to prevent the synovial fluid; and then one must saw the bone, and draw it lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and treat with poultices until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes forth, then place on it moist cloths soaked in rose oil and place on the area; and treat meanwhile the area where it belongs to the abscess, and be cautious about the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Rarely does the breakage come to the bone of the neck, and it does not often bend forth; and similarly with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that there are many mortal dispositions, and if they numb and feel well when one stretches and pricks them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient is cured, if one applies treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the back of the spine, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then take heed if the feet are softened, and if there are swellings in the hands, and on the back there is ventosity and evacuation without will; and when one has treated it above the belly button, there is evacuation without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is bent over his back and wants to settle, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: if one does not labor at all in their care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the thing is more easy.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you reward him if there is an inflamed abscess, by putting rose oil or egg yolk oil on top of the spine, until he is calmed; then put a soothing and drying emplaustre on it, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Et if some bone is severed, so cover on the wound; and take away the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is great, with a suture, then anoint with ointment, extracting flesh, until it is healed; and if the skull of the bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow", so put your pouch in your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then put the poultice and plaster on, if you need it; then strain it, and if there is a severed bone, do that, and take away the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the breaking of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, there follows a little diminution at the head; and do long and decline by degrees, and comes to the patient in pain at the spot, and punctures, and swells up what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, until you are above the breakage; and know what kind of breakage it is and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the head, so set equal to that breakage, until it is in natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is of the length, or it declines inwardly, so make the patient lie on their belly, until the restoration of that breakage appears to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it equal, so put on the poultice, then put on a plaster of wood or horn, and hold the breakage still, so that it does not move; and apply the place below the ribs, until the sides are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms there, do not touch it, until the abscess is calmed down, and put on what we have said before; then come back to the restoration, and hold it still as is necessary, if there is no bad accident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is that which is between the shoulder and the head of the arm, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of the two manners: one of which is that you take one piece of plain wood, about the size of this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two strings, and bend them up high, and make the patient sit on one chair; then throw their broken arm onto the wood, until it comes to the desired position, and has about half a covering of wood, then bend it over some heavy thing or let the attendants stretch it down below; then put the mallet on the breakage equal to your hands together, until the breakage returns as is necessary.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you make the patient sit on their haunches, and tie their hand to their neck; then instruct two attendants to have one hold what is above the breakage in their hands, and the other hold below all one string, and stretch each one to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then hold the ligament under the skinfold, and above the skinfold, and stretch each of the attendants to their share.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the skinfold is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put the ligament halfway under the armpit, and the other one towards the hollow, under the skinfold; and also if the skinfold is towards the hollow, it is necessary to put the ligament lightly, without labor, until the skinfold is even above and below, then set the skinfold as it should be, and strain it, lest abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms there, do not hold it at all for seven days, and put on a moist poultice in a warm place and with rose oil, until the abscess is calmed down; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you put the poultice on the breakage, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put the bandage, and hold it on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is in a steady state, unless something hinders it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use plasters, and put on the breakage a larger and stronger plaster than the others, with about two inches of space between each one, and so that each plaster is as large as it passes over the breakage three inches from each side; then hold on to the plasters, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the breakage, stronger and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of stars, and the constriction, as we have said, in the work that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, then let it remain tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each three days to the bandage, lest inflammation or swelling come to the place, or the numbness cannot reach the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If one approaches, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not remove the bandage except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place under the aid four cushions of equal wool, and look every hour during the day or night that the figure of the broken member does not move, or become loosened the bonds; if the accident is due to the power of medicine, and give him food as we have previously prescribed, in such a way that the food is for the most subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be noticeable.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be set in forty days from all; and then one must release and administer baths and medicaments of ointments to direct the joint.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is foul and stuck, then it should be released in one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm
