Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", of which one is small, and that is the one that supports the pouch; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little finger. By chance, break only the large foscile alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restorations are light, and the healing is easy; and when the great ones are broken, then the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bones that are broken alone, then it must be slightly extended and set evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great bones, then it must be stretched more strongly; and extend it on one cushion, and keep the small of the back higher than the other, and the little fingers lower than the others, so that the patient is crossed over himself, with the cushion in front of him higher than the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch the attendants' arm to the part below his hand, or to the joint, and another attendant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the mirror equal to his better form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has fragments, then place each one in its place, and if there is any fragment that holds the key, and you cannot restore it to its place, then proceed with force and osteum, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of it in a single chapter; then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there arise abscesses, then take a mixture made of rose oil and white wax that is not too hard or too soft; and apply the mixture subtly on top until the abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerote, and put an embalming powder made of mill powder with a lot of egg white, after which put in stars, and let the star be more forceful on the edge, slightly larger than the others; and know that there should be six stars or arms in various dispositions: whether the briseure is on one bone, or two; and hold it tighter above the briseure than elsewhere, and always less far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the drapes that are above the briseure be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the threads, with which it is strained, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member in hot water, until those itchings are calmed; and let the member not at all rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the stretching, and if the ligament is damaged and the bones are separated, or something similar, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you soften it a little bit, and let it be thus for some days, until the swelling comes, and then strain.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not separate them for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or, around, then bind his hands to his neck, and make his necks even, and beware of movement and getting up, and sleep on his back; and know that this bruise is restored in 30 days or 35, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	(None)
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and among the fingers, there are many breakages, and but few abscesses come.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bent, then it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged and sit straight in front of him evenly; then place his hand on the extended cloth, and extend the attendants' fingers, and set them even with the mire, until they are well joined; and put a plaster and poultices, if abscesses do not come, then put a stitch according to the quality of the linen; and be wrapped in one poultice of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the knuckle of the finger, then make a sphere of drapes, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken finger; and then strain with a long drape, and let the stitch be as soft as the flesh of the hand, and strain, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the end, then it is necessary that you put a stitch on top, and another one below in the finger, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind everything around the hand, and stop the strap between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of our fingers, except for the thumb, then set it even, as is necessary; and bind with the finger, and see if you put a straight small stitch to lift the break, and does not move; and if the break is in other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, then set it even, and bind with the healthy finger that comes after; or you bind them all together, just holding what's worth it, or you put a stitch on top, like on the thumb; and take care in the restoration and disposition of abscesses hot, and address what comes, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	(None)
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the ankle is often broken, and one can see when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that you tie one strap above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each attendant stretches his strap to his part evenly; and that is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the tailbone, then one of the ligaments points towards the fingernail, and the other ligaments are below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then one ligament is under the knee and the other extends downward; then place the mirrors equal to his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster and tie it, lest abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess hot, then let it be calmed and then return to your work and your care; the binding is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the break with a double-layered bandage of three or four layers, and remove any superfluous parts; then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the nail, and insert a long thread between the tailbone and the leg, under the knee from below, and let the end of the thread come out on top; then wrap the bandage around the leg and tailbone, then place three or four stays on the break; then start binding firmly; as you go up the break, loosen the bind; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you have inserted between the leg and tailbone, and tie three stays above, then return to the bottom at the end of the thread, until it comes out under the foot; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it so, and let there be no abscess or swelling or similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is, then dislodge it and set straight what comes forth, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that pinch, then one must split it open, if possible; and if not, then one must cut through the ligament, and pull forward; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And any time the case is broken, one puts in splints, as in an arm or leg; nonetheless, in this restoration made it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the case is restored in one day, or perhaps less or more, according to the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Knows that in the hollow of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it's only a split or a hole, and it happens to all wounds, and without wound, and that seems quite well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one sets equal those things which are torn to their joints, as long as it can be assembled; then put an ointment, and put in a rounded splint, if you need it, and strain it as it should be, then reward all the dispositions we have said for other breaks, just like aposteme heat and similar things; and put what is needed to each accident, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Knows that in the leg there are two bones, for which one is called by right "malleoli", and the other is called "fibula"; and it happens to all breaking like it comes to the arm, and therefore the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the work is complete. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and is easily seen; and turns below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer an extension, and set it evenly, and bind the splints equally; but always, if the break is ugly and there are many pieces, let the extension be smaller and lighter; and stretch according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two pieces of split wood that correspond to the length of the leg from one end to the other, and wrap them around the leg with bandages on top and bottom, and tie it in the middle as well; and so the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and some people wrap a wooden splint along the length of the leg, and it is made of wood, and one puts the leg to prevent movement, and properly does what is needed for the break or wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is aposteme heat or another accident; and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breakage, but sometimes the bones of the foot do break and the toes are a little bent, and it's nothing more than some slight movement.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot break and you see those bones overlapping each other, then set the patient's foot on the ground, as if it were going to walk; and then put your own foot on top of his, at the place where the bones are lifted up; then press down so they return to their places; then apply an ointment and cover with a cloth on top, and put underneath the belly of the foot a small tablet with two full cheeks; then tighten it to the foot accordingly; and when you have wrapped bandages around, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days will have passed, then loosen the binding, for you will find the bones equalized, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some broken toes, then restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on each broken toe a splint according to its length, and make it slightly wider, then place underneath the foot that tablet which I mentioned, and strain it accordingly; and if there are three or four or more broken toes, then put a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and strain the tablet underneath the foot; and let it be so that the ventral part of the foot is held firmly.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it's necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, as we have said; and treat each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the thumb bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the finger of man is broken, or of woman, restore it thus as we have said in the bones of the hare; and these breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and use there, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies more than one disposition to the right way of restoration; then understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and pour it into the penis; then wrap bandages around it, and let it be for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaks with wounds
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, even if it is great, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, and the wounds that we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then keep it moist with vinegar, if you have nothing else; then begin again to restore the break in that same hour or day, lest apostemes come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess forms there, then let the restoration wait until the ninth day, so that the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing above the skin's surface, then it is necessary that you set it slightly to your hands, at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suited to set equal with your hands, then reamend this instrument made of iron, which has 8 or 9 inches length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the surgeon to take 3 or 4, according to what he needs in each breaking treatment; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend much under compression on the limb at your work, and be sharp before, and thick from halfway forward thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palinche", therefore it is necessary that the curved key be placed on top of the apparent bone; and bind it once, until it regains its shape, and let them be equal to one another.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the top of the bone, until the instruments have possession.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, or chisel or saw, to your ability; then ream out what remains in the bone of roughness and small scraps.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reduced and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So it is in its place, then wet the linen cloth with black stiptic wine, and properly cover it; and do not put on the wound cerote or anything else that has oil, lest you cause infection and corruption; then administer the poultice when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the breakage.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil consequences may come, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it is not necessary to put on poultices; but wrap around, in place of poultices, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see the boil after one or two days to enlarge on the wound, then remove everything you put on top with all vinegar and put healing unguent for wounds, such as four-herb ointment and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb two times a day, morning and evening, until it is bound up and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the bow-like shape runs down slowly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but instead returns to being bowed, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which reason it is necessary that you cleanse the wound with a tent, and remove all these devitalized pieces that bring about that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is written in its chapter beforehand.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens on the member, such as the hip or shoulder bone, and other similar great bones, do not pull it at all, for many times death ensues, but leave it until it has healed; perhaps it will fall out after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come on the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see this after the healing of a break, especially when it is near the jointure, and it is a sad thing to behold the shape of the limb; and by chance the limb cannot perform its natural actions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if we are fresh: administer stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, acaica, and similar others, in such a way that you take some of these things or all together, and mix them with black wine or with abundant urine or with oil; and put it on the boil at night in cauldrons, and strain it well, and do not remove it for several days; then remove it, and begin another one, until the swelling is gone; or you can bind it with a piece of cloth well made; for the properties of cloth are such that they remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then cut it away, and make the superfluity apparent; or have it done by any razor, until it is removed, and cure it as long as it remains unhealed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone break is restored and the limb remains weak and subtle afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not allow the nourishment to reach the limb; or because of excessive swelling; or because of great movements, but not at its proper time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and give their body nourishment until the blood is multiplied in them; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and the swelling often subsides with warm water, until the nourishment flows to the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone appears, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those foolish people who say that one must break the limb all over again; many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great evils come from it, and by chance death itself; however, if the nodulations and tortures are fresh, then it is necessary to rise them with warm water, or cook soft herbs such as vervain leaves, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as one made with dyaquilon well done, and take the mucilage of vervain and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take figs that are fatty, and grind them with flax seed, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the lump is removed by constant and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be gentle movement to each member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is inflamed and hardened like stone, and it needs to be cut with iron, then it must be covered just to the bone, slightly incising finely; and put sense and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	There is no sentence to translate in this case, as "Ci encomence li livres des dislocations" appears to be the title or heading of a section within the text, rather than a sentence to be translated.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then one must immediately restore it.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the swelling grows, and by chance if it is reset with pain at the swelling; therefore it is not good to move it until it has subsided: many times bring shame and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, make the patient sicker, then leave him, until the abscesses are appeased; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then reposition it gently, and care for each member as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: or they are slightly removed from their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot be held, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in a few positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you should reposition it quickly, without delaying; and in such a way that the attendants hold the patient's head, and pour the mirror's sap from one of their hands into the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are free to make equal; and instruct the patient to soften his jawbones and move them all around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror places it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return, even if they are the two jawbones together, then raise them with warm water and oil, until you gently reset them; nor delay in returning, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well with a sense of softening, then place damp cloths on them in a poultice made of rose oil and wax, then bind lightly with moist bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his legs be positioned between two cushions, so that he does not move to either side, nor does he make an effort to speak, but takes light food, until the pains are gone, and the jaws are numb; and then eat what he wants lightly, and does not worry about opening his mouth to eat or drink, as long as the jaw is well numb and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not converted back to their position, then fever and usual habit come to pass, and by chance, solution of the belly, and by chance, vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign of death; and often the person who has it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot dislocate from the front into its continuity and towards the chest, and is dislocated at times to the back, and it is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, stretches out his arms; and then presses the joint firmly with his palm, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and tighten; and the leg which is towards the cut cannot dislocate; if not, and if it does happen to dislocate at any time, then reset it back to its place, just as we said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and tighten, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the same procedure is followed for bringing back the leg from the shoulder, when it becomes separated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways: the one that dislocates at the base of the shoulder blade below; and the second that dislocates at the part of the spine; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inwardly for the arm pits.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is a blow or crushing, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it has dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you inspect it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation occurs when it goes down towards the shoulder blade, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them manifest diversity; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and below the shoulder blade, touching the top of the shoulder, just as if it were an ox; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their neck nor move with any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not to be restored except when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the attendants lift the patient's hand up high, then place their fingers below the armpit, and lift the jointure with force to its place; and the attendants lift the hand, and stretch it out high, then put it back down; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within four days after, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and the assistant should gently soften and soothe, as a decoction of alder, fenugreek, and melilotus in water is made, and brought forth. Then the patient should be placed on their back, and an equal wool pad should be placed underneath the shoulder blade, not too soft nor too hard, then place the mirror at the heel of the patient, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and draw out the patient's hand; and another assistant should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downward. The shoulder now returns immediately, and if you see that you should do this: and it is that you make someone present who is larger than the patient; and be straight towards the costard, and push the patient's shoulder underneath the shoulder blade of the patient, and lift the shoulder up so that the patient hangs in the air; and another assistant should draw out the patient's hand downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can lift with him something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one also remedies it in another way: thus take a long iron rod and place it on the ground, so that the head is as tall as a pistol, neither too big nor too small; then have him placed under the patient, but with the cloth wrapped soft above, and the patient's hand will be stretched down below in this form, and the jointure will return to its place quickly.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie it on top of the wooden beam with a soft cloth, so that the wood does not hurt the patient, then place it under the pillow of the patient; and stretch your arm over the long rod, and tie the assistant on top of the rod, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on one shoulder of an easel wide, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, in whatever way it may be, then it is necessary that you place under the pillow a sphere of equal wool, then put the poultice wrapped with powder from the mill, with incense and an egg yolk, on all the shoulder and around, then strain the poultice under the pillow comfortably, and turn the cloth over the poultice, and enfold the hand in its own neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he rest a little, until the members are comforted, for he will heal more quickly; and then let him rest again after five days or seven, and move him; and if he is firm and has not been softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply cauterizations to three pores, as shown before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and after seven days he still does not hold, and the joint will not lift his arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is near the chest or breast or behind, is caused by impulse and stretching of hands, and another method is administered; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes swelling in the member and tardiness of movement, then have the patient take many baths until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is displaced at points, and returns at points; and if it is displaced from all sides, and especially before and behind, and the dislocation is not corrected, for one can see it well and feel it well; and displace according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person with good health, so you can see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joints are stiff and cannot bend the arm, nor touch their shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the abscesses do not come to life again, for if the abscesses were to form again, it would be grievous to reset; and by chance it cannot be fully reset from all sides, especially when it is behind; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance it brings death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such when it can be reset that you stretch his hand to your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and his hands of the mirror according to the shoulder around, above, and below, and push the joint to its crevices together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and pushes the shoulder which is displaced from its place at the root of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and thus two ministers extend the arm, and hold it steady two ministers, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm on both sides, having wrapped a cloth double long and wide; and when the doctor has joined the jointure to her hand, oil it with some oil to soften the jointure, then bind the jointure firmly, until it returns; and when it is back in place, put on plaster powder mixed with egg, and strain it firmly, and leave the arm at the neck of the patient for a few days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the poultice and the bandage, and let it be thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels grief after the joint is reset, and it moves, then bathe and stroke him well, and press until he is soothed; or you put some sheep's fat on the jointure, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, stroke the jointure temperately, then put the fat back on, and then enter the bath; and thus do it two or three times until he is healed; and if you see, then put some vetch seed, moist and warmed with butter, and strain it on him; so he will return to his disposition.
li dislocation de la main	Hand dislocation
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The jointure of the hand dislocated, and the return is light, more than the other joints Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place promptly, in the same time that it is dislocated, so long as the swelling remains or an abscess forms hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is that you put the patient's hand on a table, and stretch out his fingers, and let the doctor place it even, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the jointure, and hold it until it recovers. However, it is necessary for you to look if it is well in its place; then put the patient's hand back on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then the patient places the back of their hand on the table, and the physician puts their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If she returns now, it's well If not, then he should strain soothing poultices on abscesses and let him be thus without reoccurring.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he can't endure it, and you can't put it in its place after some days, then the joint remains twisted; and it's not necessary for the patient to do anything else as long as his hand is numb, and he can't strain any part at all: thus know that the nerves are strained, or the arteries; if there is no other remedy than to strain by applying fire cauterization around the case, and perhaps nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the ointment that we have said, then strain and leave it five days, then release and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, then soak the water hot, and rub it until he is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the two tendons of the hand are dislocated to each part, sometimes on the back of the palm or belly; then they are bent, and push the dislocation towards your pouches as long as it revives, then hold the head of the tendon and bend it towards the part where it is disconnected; and leave it for two days, and then put it in its place that day; and bind it with a bandage, just as we have said, and loosen it from one day to another, and make it move, and rebind the nut; and do this often, until it is straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do so as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the hip of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hip of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, then there is no remedy, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	Et li signes si est that the evacuations spring forth without will, nor can they be held, and many times a certain member is softened, or two arms or both legs; and many times the shin bone changes into four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you reward if gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no care nor recovery throughout.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussions or similar things, the ancient methods of cures say with great words, where there is not much benefit in all; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositis that comes to the front of the chest, there is no intelligence nor health; and also that which comes directly in both sides, and one can only cure the fire that comes properly to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in an equal position, and have a strain under him, so he does not get hurt; then place two tissons in the ground, one at the head and the other at the feet, and tie one string between the straps of the patient's legs, and another between the hips, and thighs, and ankles; and two ministers know the strings, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two tissons; and be well closed, the tissons as we have said, and the mirrors place their palms on the spine firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a board three arms long, and hollow out the bottom part of it, and have the patient sit on the side, and put the head of the board under the part that shows, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and place the mirrors at the feet on the other end of the board, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see, do so also to the one who turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And do so that you place two tongs at the head of the patient one arm long, and two others towards the feet, with a palm's width between each tong, above and below; and have one pertus in each tong where the turning takes place, and let the tongs be firmly on the ground so they don't move; and between each pair of tongs, put one turning tong, whereupon the tendons turn, and have two small tongs one palm long to turn the turning; then tie the cord that is among the straps at the head towards the head, and the other cord at the feet towards the other tongue, and each servant turns their tongue to all the cord, and the master makes the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equal, he puts on desiccating plaster with an abundance of egg whites, and then binds, and then takes a small iron tool, three digits long, to reposition the seat of the gilbositis and the part of the spine, then binds with a bandage, as we have said, and uses gentle nursing care until the patient is healed; and if nothing comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer soothing and calming medicines, with the tool we mentioned before; and sometimes one should administer a piece of pumice stone, and sometimes there appears in the rear part of the spine on the back, and think that it is dislocation; but it is the bone that opens up, so one should not have presumption: for it may bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come to dislocations, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to .iiii. parts: inward and outward, and before and behind; and more inward than outward, and less dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of its dislocation is that when one joins the ailing leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens up more in the patient's knee than in the healthy one, and the ailing patient cannot double their knee over the fire; and the swelling is located near the inflamed aposteme, because the head of the hip comes away.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens outward is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it happens before is that he is well in his leg according to fulfillment; however, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot beforehand, and retains his urine, and swells with anger, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind is that he cannot straighten his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and the head of the hip is at the level below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this likeness of dislocation are that you restore whether the dislocation is old and it remains according to its disposition, if there is no care; and it is not necessary that he have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the three kinds of dislocation, you hasten to return the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it will come back, and there is no need for another care.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort à II mains, ou à I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main dessus en tel manièr qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrene d’un souef lién sur la cuixe; et uns autres tienne le chief du lié; et estendent amont et aval tout à une fois, tant que le malaide soit levé de terre à une fois, et demeure pendant.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to the three likenesses, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to put a cure on its likeness. When the dislocation is in the middle, it is necessary that you support the patient on their side, then place the strap on the root of the hollow, and the lever that is below the angle, then stretch the strap up towards the angle, and towards the forefoot; then take another minister's arms, and embrace the thick part of the hollow patient, and stretch it far away: thus it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bind it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two legs of the patient together with a soft cord on the two heels and calves, and the sick leg be stretched two digits longer than the others; then let it be hung from the head of a tree, and let it be above the earth two arms long; then instruct the servant to wrap the chief of the crotch, and let another servant stand with the patient, tightly wrapping the crotch, for the joints are now returning quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the rear, then the patient lies down as we have said in those who have gilbositeit, and stretch the cord properly on the sick leg, and also on the hip; then put two torches, one at the head and one at the feet, then stick the torch between the crotch of the patient inside the shape; and have planted moist cloths all around, so that the patient does not get hurt, then each servant spreads out towards him, and the surgeon puts an equal amount of dislocation to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If she returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put her on the bed, and press thus as we have said in the gilbosity, and place the patient on the natural side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is before, it is necessary to stretch the diseased leg hastily, and according to what I have said; and put the physician's hand on the angry diseased hip, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
